Political conflicts often involve different prioritization of these foundations. Liberals prioritize care and fairness; conservatives add loyalty, authority, and sanctity. This creates moral matrices that are mutually incomprehensible—not just disagreement but inability to understand how opponents can believe what they do.

The friend-enemy distinction activates the loyalty/betrayal foundation intensely. Enemies are traitors to the group, disloyal to sacred values, subversive of legitimate authority. *(Haidt, "The Righteous Mind," 2012)*

**4. Cognitive Biases Supporting Enmity**

Numerous cognitive biases maintain friend-enemy distinctions:

- **Confirmation bias**: Seeking evidence confirming enemies are dangerous, ignoring disconfirming evidence
- **Fundamental attribution error**: Attributing enemy behavior to their nature ("they're evil"), our behavior to circumstances ("we had no choice")
- **Group-serving bias**: Crediting in-group successes to ability, failures to circumstances; reverse for out-group
- **False consensus effect**: Overestimating how many people share your views, underestimating legitimacy of opposition
- **Hostile attribution bias**: Interpreting ambiguous enemy actions as hostile when same action by friend seen as benign
- **Biased assimilation**: Same evidence makes both sides more convinced they're right and enemies are wrong

These biases are not mere errors but functional for group cohesion—they maintain solidarity by preventing recognition of enemy humanity and legitimate grievances. *(Haidt, "The Emotional Dog and Its Rational Tail")*

**5. Social Identity Theory**

Self-esteem partly derived from status of groups we belong to. Therefore:
- Motivated to see in-group positively
- Motivated to see out-group negatively (boosts relative status)
- Social comparisons create competitive dynamic even absent material conflicts
- Threat to group threatens individual identity, provoking defensive reactions

This explains why trivial differences can become basis for intense conflict—the issue isn't really the difference but the need to maintain positive social identity through comparison. *(Tajfel and Turner, "An Integrative Theory of Intergroup Conflict," 1979)*

**6. Realistic Conflict Theory**

Competition over scarce resources creates intergroup hostility. Muzafer Sherif's Robber's Cave experiments showed:
- Groups compete for prizes → hostility, stereotyping, violence
- Superordinate goals requiring cooperation → reduction in hostility

Suggests friend-enemy distinctions may be manufactured even when no real conflict exists, but become real through self-fulfilling prophecy. *(Sherif et al., "Intergroup Conflict and Cooperation: The Robbers Cave Experiment," 1961)*

**7. Collective Narcissism**

Group-level narcissism—belief that in-group deserves special recognition but doesn't receive it—predicts:
- Hypersensitivity to perceived slights from out-groups
- Aggressive response to criticism
- Conspiracy theories about enemies undermining group
- Support for aggressive leaders who promise to restore group greatness

National narcissism ("Make America Great Again," Russian restoration of empire, Chinese "century of humiliation") creates enemies who must be defeated to restore rightful status. *(Golec de Zavala et al., "Collective Narcissism and Its Social Consequences," 2013)*

---

### Historical Case Studies: Friend-Enemy Distinctions in Action

Theory must be tested against historical reality. How have friend-enemy distinctions actually operated in political history?

**Case 1: The Wars of Religion (16th-17th Centuries)**

The Protestant-Catholic conflicts demonstrate:

**Escalation from contingent to absolute enmity**: Initially theological disputes transformed into existential conflicts. Each side came to see the other as not merely wrong but damned, not merely opponents but demonic enemies of God. The Thirty Years' War (1618-1648) became total war destroying much of Central Europe.

**Internal enemy dynamics**: Both sides hunted heretics within their territories. Spanish Inquisition, Protestant witch hunts created internal enemies whose hidden presence demanded vigilance. Friend-enemy boundary cuts through families, cities, regions.

**Schmittian analysis**: This illustrates how religious distinction became political through intensity. Protestant vs. Catholic initially theological became friend-enemy through grouping people into warring camps. *(Source: Schmitt discusses this in Political Theology)*

**Resolution through de-intensification**: Peace of Westphalia (1648) ended conflict not by resolving religious dispute but by making it non-political—cuius regio, eius religio (whose realm, his religion) prevented religion from structuring international relations as friend-enemy. *(Schmitt praises this in Nomos of the Earth)*

**Lesson**: Existential enmities can be transformed by refusing to let particular distinctions structure the political, but requires agreement to depoliticize the issue.

**Case 2: French Revolution and Terror (1789-1794)**

The Revolution demonstrates:

**Creation of internal enemies**: "Enemies of the Revolution" became category for anyone opposing radical program. Aristocrats, priests, moderates, eventually rival revolutionary factions all became enemies requiring elimination.

**Expansion of enemy category**: Initially targeted aristocracy; progressively expanded to include anyone insufficiently enthusiastic. "Suspect" became status requiring internment. *(Arendt, On Revolution)*

**Terrorist logic**: Robespierre's argument that terror is virtue applied politically—destroying enemies of the people is moral necessity. "Pity is treason." Friend-enemy distinction permits no middle ground.

**Dialectic of revolution**: Each purge creates new enemies. Those who eliminated yesterday's enemies become today's enemies. Revolutionary logic consumes its children. *(Schmitt and Arendt both analyze this)*

**Constituent power**: Schmitt sees Revolution as exercise of popular constituent power through identification and destruction of enemies of popular sovereignty—king, aristocrats, enemies of the people.

**Lesson**: Friend-enemy logic without limits tends toward total domination. Terror implements the friend-enemy distinction absolutely.

**Case 3: US Civil War (1861-1865)**

Demonstrates complex friend-enemy dynamics:

**Internal vs. external enemies**: Were Confederates enemies of USA or rebellious citizens? Legal ambiguity about their status. Lincoln treated them as rebels (internal enemies) not foreign enemies, but war still total.

**Slavery as friend-enemy issue**: Incompatible social systems in same political unit. Schmitt would argue this illustrates need for homogeneity—Union could not persist half-slave, half-free.

**Reconstruction dilemma**: After military defeat, how to treat former enemies? Punish as traitors or reconcile as fellow citizens? Failure to decisively resolve created Jim Crow and century of racial enmity.

**Moral vs. existential enmity**: North increasingly framed conflict as moral (slavery is evil) vs. South's existential framing (defending way of life). Schmittian analysis: Moralizing made conflict more absolute.

**Lesson**: Internal enemies more dangerous than external because victory doesn't resolve their status. Must be either expelled, eliminated, or truly reconciled.

**Case 4: Totalitarian Regimes (Nazi Germany, Soviet Union, Maoist China)**

These represent the ultimate implementation of Schmittian friend-enemy logic:

**Total mobilization**: Every aspect of life subordinated to struggle against enemies. No neutral space, no private sphere. Total politicization in Schmitt's sense.

**Ever-present enemies**: Ideology requires enemies to justify totalitarian control. As external enemies defeated, must discover/create internal enemies. Kulaks, wreckers, saboteurs, cosmopolitans, counter-revolutionaries, hidden traitors.

**Biological/class enemies**: Nazi racial antisemitism and Stalinist class enemies make enmity structural and hereditary. Born as enemy, die as enemy.

**Perfect homogeneity as goal**: Totalitarianism attempts to realize Schmitt's vision of complete homogeneity through elimination of all difference. Genocide and gulags implement friend-enemy distinction absolutely. *(Arendt, Origins of Totalitarianism)*

**Institutionalization of terror**: Secret police, informant networks, show trials, concentration camps institutionalize friend-enemy identification. Society atomized through fear of being labeled enemy.

**Lesson**: Schmitt's political theology, taken to its logical conclusion, produces totalitarian horror. Absolute friend-enemy distinction permits no limits on power.

**Case 5: Israel-Palestine**

Contemporary conflict illustrating intractable friend-enemy dynamics:

**Competing existential narratives**: Each side views conflict as existential. Israelis: Jewish state necessary for survival after Holocaust; surrounding Arab states seek destruction. Palestinians: colonization threatens their existence as people with national rights.

**Security dilemma**: Israeli security measures (checkpoints, wall, Gaza blockade) appear as Palestinian oppression; Palestinian resistance (intifadas, rockets) appears as existential threat to Israel. Each side's defense is other side's aggression.

**Martyrdom and retaliation**: Each side's martyrs demand vengeance. Memorial practices keep past enmities alive and justify present violence.

**Outbidding dynamics**: Political leaders compete to be toughest on enemy. Israeli right outbids center on security; Palestinian factions compete in resistance. Moderates lose credibility.

**One-state vs. two-state**: Fundamental disagreement about whether shared state possible or enemy status permanent. Two-state acknowledges enmity but seeks separation; one-state would require transforming enemies into fellow citizens.

**International dimensions**: Regional and global powers turn local conflict into proxy for broader friend-enemy alignments (US-Israel vs. Iran-Syria-Hezbollah).

**Lesson**: Without credible mechanism to transform enemies into partners, conflict can persist indefinitely through self-reinforcing dynamics.

**Case 6: Rwandan Genocide (1994)**

Demonstrates horrifying rapidity of friend-enemy escalation:

**Constructed divisions**: Hutu-Tutsi distinction created by Belgian colonial policy, not ancient tribal enmity. Shows friend-enemy can be manufactured.

**Radio propaganda**: "Hate radio" (RTLM) systematically dehumanized Tutsi as "cockroaches" requiring extermination. Media crucial for mass mobilization.

**Neighbor killing neighbor**: Genocide carried out by ordinary citizens against former friends and neighbors. Social pressure and fear made participation seemingly obligatory.

**Speed of escalation**: From political assassination of president to industrial-scale genocide in weeks. Shows how quickly contingent conflicts can become absolute enmity.

**Bystander effect**: International community watched passively. Debate about whether "genocide" or "tribal conflict" affected willingness to intervene.

**Post-genocide**: How to reconstitute society when neighbors murdered neighbors? Gacaca courts attempted restorative justice, but trauma persists.

**Lesson**: Friend-enemy distinctions can be activated with terrifying speed. Dehumanization enables ordinary people to commit extraordinary evil.

---

## Implicit Friend-Enemy Distinctions: De Facto Structures

Many systems embody friend-enemy logic without explicitly theorizing it. This section analyzes implicit manifestations:

### Capitalist Market Economies

Markets appear neutral, governed by impersonal laws of supply and demand. Yet Marx revealed deep enmities:

**Structural antagonism**: Bourgeoisie and proletariat have objectively opposed interests. Capitalists profit from workers' exploitation; workers benefit from limiting exploitation. Not personal animosity but structural position creates enmity.

**Class consciousness**: Workers must recognize class enemies to organize politically. Liberal ideology obscures class conflict by individualizing (everyone responsible for own success) or economizing (just market competition).

**De facto friendenemies**: Capitalists compete with each other (enemies) but unite against workers when class interests threatened (friends). Workers compete for jobs but share interest in resisting exploitation.

**Primitive accumulation**: Capitalism emerges from violent dispossession—enclosures, colonialism, slavery. Friend-enemy logic operates in extraction of value from enemies (colonized, enslaved, dispossessed).

**Modern manifestations**: "Class warfare" rhetoric reveals enmity: Tax cuts for rich vs. social programs for poor frames politics as zero-sum. Corporate capture of government operates through friend-enemy (business-friendly policy vs. regulation benefiting workers/consumers).

**Implicit Schmittianism**: Neoliberalism's "There is no alternative" (TINA) seeks to depoliticize economy by presenting market outcomes as natural law rather than political decisions. But crises reveal political nature—bank bailouts vs. austerity for masses shows who are friends (finance capital) vs. enemies (working class).

### Liberal Democracy's Hidden Exclusions

Liberalism claims universalism but operates through hidden friend-enemy distinctions:

**Founding exclusions**: Liberal democracies founded on exclusion of women, non-property-owners, racial minorities, colonized peoples from "We the people." Schmitt's critique: Liberal universalism conceals particular interests of those who belong.

**Formal equality, substantive inequality**: Equal rights before law compatible with extreme inequality of resources and power. Friends (propertied, educated, connected) benefit from formal equality; enemies (dispossessed, marginalized, excluded) cannot exercise nominal rights.

**Normality and deviance**: Liberal tolerance requires drawing line between acceptable and unacceptable—what Milton Fanon calls "repressive tolerance." Must tolerate diverse views within range, but must not tolerate "intolerance." Who decides? Hidden exercise of power determines what counts as beyond pale.

**Emergency powers**: Every liberal democracy has provisions for suspending liberties in emergencies. State of exception built into liberal order. Schmitt: This proves liberal legalism ultimately rests on sovereign decision.

**Implicit homogeneity requirement**: "Multiculturalism" and "diversity" celebrated within limits. Deep pluralism (conflicting ultimate values, incompatible ways of life) not really accommodated. Requires assimilation to liberal values or exclusion.

**Criminalization of politics**: Liberal order treats genuine political opposition as crime. Radical movements criminalized (communism, anarchism, terrorism), reducing politics to administration. Those who reject system become enemies rather than opponents.

### Nation-States as Friend-Enemy Machines

The modern nation-state implicitly embodies friend-enemy logic:

**Borders**: Physical manifestation of friend-enemy. Who can cross? Citizenship determines who belongs. Border controls enact violent exclusion.

**Nationalism**: Construction of national identity requires external enemies (other nations) and internal homogeneity (shared national character). National myths often center on conflicts with enemies.

**Military and police**: State institutions whose purpose is applying violence against external enemies (military) and internal enemies (police). Monopoly on legitimate violence (Weber) = monopoly on deciding who can be killed.

**Immigration and naturalization**: Legal processes of determining who can become friend from enemy. Assimilation requirements, citizenship tests, loyalty oaths all mechanisms for screening out enemies.

**Enemy aliens and sedition**: In wartime, nationals of enemy states become enemy aliens subject to internment. Sedition and treason laws target internal enemies—those who aid external enemies or subvert from within.

**Passport and visa systems**: Global regime of movement control that presumes enemy status—must prove you're not threat to be permitted entry. Privileged passports (US, EU) vs. stigmatized (Syria, Afghanistan) show hierarchy of enmity.

**Colonial legacies**: Postcolonial states inherit friend-enemy structures from colonial rule—borders arbitrary, often cutting across ethnic groups, creating enduring conflicts. Colonized peoples were enemy Others; independence doesn't erase these divisions.

---

### Religious Systems and Sacred Enmity

Religious traditions structure friend-enemy through sacred/profane distinctions:

**Abrahamic monotheisms**: Believers vs. infidels/heretics creates fundamental division. Salvation depends on correct belief; wrong believers threaten not just social order but cosmic order. Enemy's existence an affront to God.

**Dar al-Islam vs. Dar al-Harb**: Islamic jurisprudence traditionally divides world into "house of Islam" (territory under Islamic law) and "house of war" (territory to be brought under Islam). Creates perpetual friend-enemy structuring of world, though historical practice more complex. *(Khadduri, War and Peace in the Law of Islam)*

**Christian just war tradition**: Augustine's theology permits violence against enemies of God and justice. Crusades, religious wars, missionary colonization all justified through friend-enemy identification with divine will. Enemy becomes demon, war becomes spiritual combat.

**Excommunication and anathema**: Religious power to exclude from community of believers. Catholic excommunication, Jewish herem, Islamic takfir all mark individuals as religious enemies, often with civil consequences. Social death through religious exclusion.

**Sectarian violence**: Intra-religious divisions (Sunni-Shia, Catholic-Protestant, Orthodox-heterodox) often more intense than inter-religious. Heretics more dangerous than infidels because they pervert truth from within. Friend-enemy boundary within religious community more unstable, requiring constant policing.

**Secularism as enemy**: For religious fundamentalists, secularism itself becomes enemy threatening sacred order. Liberal separation of church/state seen as attack on religion. Creates friend-enemy based on acceptance vs. rejection of religious authority in public life.

---

### Economic Structures and Class Enmity

Beyond Marx's overt class analysis, economic systems implicitly structure enmities:

**Creditor vs. debtor**: One of oldest friend-enemy dynamics. Creditor has power over debtor; debtor resents creditor. Debt creates relationships of domination. Ancient prohibitions on usury, medieval anti-Semitism (associated Jews with moneylending), modern debt resistance movements all express debtor enmity toward creditors. *(Graeber, Debt: The First 5,000 Years)*

**Landlord vs. tenant**: Land ownership creates structural enmity. Those who own land can extract rent from those who need it. Peasant revolts, land reform movements, rent strikes express this enmity. Schmitt's concept of Nomos (land-taking) recognizes primordial importance of land in political enmity.

**Employer vs. employee**: Wage labor creates antagonistic relationship even absent personal animosity. Employer profits by minimizing labor costs; workers benefit from maximizing them. Zero-sum within firm even if positive-sum economy-wide.

**Producer vs. consumer**: Producers want high prices; consumers want low prices. Market competition supposed to mediate, but producers organize (monopolies, cartels) while consumers more difficult to organize. Consumer protection movements express recognition of structural conflict.

**Finance vs. productive capital**: Rentier vs. entrepreneur. Finance extracts value without producing; productive capital actually makes things. Different fractions of capital have divergent interests. Fascism often mobilizes "productive" national capital against "parasitic" international finance (often coded antisemitic).

**Global North vs. Global South**: Dependency theory and world-systems analysis reveal how core economies exploit periphery. "Unequal exchange" transfers value from South to North. Anti-colonial movements recognize imperial powers as enemies extracting wealth.

**Gig economy and platform capitalism**: Platform owners vs. workers creates new structural enmity. Uber vs. drivers, Amazon vs. warehouse workers, etc. Algorithmic management obscures but doesn't eliminate antagonism.

---

### Gender and Sexuality: Enmity in Intimate Relations

Feminist theory reveals friend-enemy logic in gender/sexuality:

**Patriarchy as structural enmity**: Radical feminism (MacKinnon, Dworkin) argues men as class are enemies of women as class. Not personal hatred but structural domination. All men benefit from patriarchy; all women suffer from it.

**Public vs. private**: Liberal distinction conceals domestic violence, marital rape, reproductive control as "private matters." Feminist slogan "personal is political" reveals friend-enemy operating in supposedly depoliticized intimate sphere.

**Compulsory heterosexuality**: Adrienne Rich argues heterosexuality enforced through violence against queer people. Heterosexual nuclear family as institution requires policing of sexual enemies (homosexuals, trans people, gender non-conformers).

**TERF wars**: Trans-Exclusionary Radical Feminists treat trans women as male enemies invading women's spaces. Essentialist view of womanhood creates trans people as enemies of feminism. Friend-enemy within feminist movement.

**Incel ideology**: Involuntarily celibate men construct women as enemies denying them deserved sexual access. Women's sexual autonomy perceived as attack on male entitlement. Produces misogynist violence against women as enemy class.

**Sex work debates**: Carceral feminism treats sex workers as victims, Johns/pimps as enemies requiring police intervention. Sex worker activists argue this creates harmful enmity, that real enemies are police and anti-sex-work feminists.

**Reproductive politics**: Pro-choice vs. pro-life creates absolute friend-enemy. Each side views other as existential threat (to women's autonomy vs. to fetal life). No middle ground possible when framed as life-or-death.

---

### Ecology and Species-Being: Post-Human Enmities

Environmental politics creates new friend-enemy formations:

**Humans vs. nature**: Enlightenment modernity constructs nature as resource to be dominated. Bacon's "torture nature for its secrets," Descartes's mechanistic nature. Nature becomes enemy to be conquered through science/technology. *(Merchant, The Death of Nature)*

**Deep ecology**: Reverses human/nature enmity—humans are enemy species destroying Earth. Misanthropic strand views human extinction as positive for biosphere. Creates friend-enemy where non-human nature are friends, humans enemies.

**Eco-fascism**: Combines ecological concern with nationalism/racism. "We" must defend sacred homeland against immigrant enemies who overpopu

late and pollute. Climate refugees as invasion. Malthusian logic identifies poor/non-white as enemies of sustainable planet. Tragic mass shootings in Christchurch, El Paso motivated by eco-fascist ideology.

**Climate justice vs. fossil capital**: Movement identifies fossil fuel industry as enemy of human survival. Divestment, blockades, sabotage express this enmity. Industry portrays environmentalists as enemies of jobs/growth. *(Malm, How to Blow Up a Pipeline)*

**Anthropocene politics**: Recognition of human geological agency creates questions about who "we" are. Which humans responsible for climate change? Industrial capitalism, not humanity as such. But discourse of "Anthropocene" risks obscuring differential responsibility, treating all humans as equally enemy of planet. *(Haraway prefers "Capitalocene")*

**Multispecies justice**: Efforts to extend political standing to non-humans (animals, ecosystems, rivers). Who speaks for non-human friends? How to include them in political community? Schmitt's friend-enemy assumes human groups; ecological politics transcends this.

---

## Power: Mechanisms, Modalities, and Transformations

Having analyzed friend-enemy distinctions, we must examine power more systematically. How does power operate through friend-enemy distinctions? What forms does it take?

### Dimensions of Power

Political theory distinguishes multiple dimensions/faces of power:

**First dimension (Dahl): Power as decision-making**

A has power over B to the extent A can get B to do something B wouldn't otherwise do. Observable in concrete decisions and conflicts. Pluralist view: Power dispersed among competing groups who win some decisions, lose others.

Friend-enemy application: Power is ability to impose costs on enemies, provide benefits to friends. Measured through victory in concrete conflicts over policy.

**Second dimension (Bachrach & Baratz): Power as agenda-setting**

Power operates not just in decisions but in non-decisions—keeping issues off agenda. "Mobilization of bias" prevents challenges from arising. Some conflicts never become public because power prevents them from being articulated.

Friend-enemy application: Power determines what counts as political. Defining issues as "merely economic" or "private matters" depoliticizes them, preventing friend-enemy mobilization. Schmitt's critique of liberal depoliticization recognizes this dimension.

**Third dimension (Lukes): Power as preference-shaping**

Deepest form of power shapes what people want. Hegemony (Gramsci) makes domination appear natural/legitimate. People internalize interests of powerful as their own. Power most effective when invisible.

Friend-enemy application: Prevents recognition of enemies. Workers identify with capitalists against workers in other countries. Women accept patriarchy as natural. Colonized adopt colonizer's contempt for themselves. Power erases friend-enemy consciousness. *(Fanon, Black Skin, White Masks)*

**Fourth dimension (Foucault): Power as subject-constitution**

Power doesn't just constrain pre-existing subjects but produces subjects. Disciplines create docile bodies; discourses create subject positions. No sovereign power holder—power circulates through networks.

Friend-enemy application: Produces friends and enemies as subject positions. "Terrorist," "illegal alien," "welfare queen" are subject positions created by power/knowledge. Can't opt out of these positions—they're imposed by discourse.

---

### Modalities of Power Over Enemies

How does power actually operate against enemies once identified?

**1. Elimination**

Most absolute exercise of power: Physical destruction of enemies. Genocide, ethnic cleansing, political murder. Enemy problem "solved" through extermination. Totalitarian regimes' gulags and death camps. Final solution.

Historical examples: Armenian genocide, Holocaust, Rwandan genocide, Cambodia under Khmer Rouge, Stalinist great purge.

**2. Expulsion**

Physical removal of enemies from territory. Population transfers, ethnic cleansing, deportation, forced migration. Less extreme than elimination but still violent displacement.

Historical examples: Partition of India/Pakistan, Palestinian Nakba, Yugoslav wars, Trail of Tears, Soviet population transfers.

**3. Incarceration**

Imprisonment of enemies. Political prisoners, internment camps, detention centers, gulags. Removes enemies from society without killing them. Can be temporary or permanent. Creates zones of exception (Guantanamo, immigration detention, gulags).

**4. Surveillance**

Constant monitoring of enemies and potential enemies. Panopticon (Bentham/Foucault) where internalized awareness of surveillance disciplines behavior. Secret police, informant networks, NSA mass surveillance, social credit systems, predictive policing.

**5. Domination/Exploitation**

Maintaining enemies in subordinate status while extracting value. Slavery, colonialism, patriarchy, class exploitation. Enemy kept alive but subjugated. Must balance extraction with preventing rebellion.

**6. Assimilation**

Forced transformation of enemies into friends through cultural destruction. Boarding schools for indigenous children, bans on minority languages, compulsory nationalist education. Genocidal when combined with physical elimination but often operates through cultural violence alone.

**7. Legal Disempowerment**

Stripping enemies of legal protections and rights. Enemy combatants, illegal aliens, felons who lose voting rights. Create second-class legal status. Apartheid, Jim Crow, dhimmitude in Islamic states all legally instantiate enmity.

**8. Economic Immiseration**

Impoverishing enemies through economic policy. Sanctions, blockades, predatory lending, structural adjustment, austerity. Economic warfare makes enemies dependent, unable to resist. IMF/World Bank structural adjustment operates this way against Global South.

**9. Symbolic Degradation**

Humiliation, insult, stigmatization of enemies. Hate speech, dehumanizing propaganda, forcing visible markers (yellow star, pink triangle). Damages enemies' dignity and social standing without physical violence—though often escalates to physical violence.

**10. Bureaucratic Exclusion**

Excluding enemies through administrative procedures. Impossible documentation requirements, Kafkaesque processes, arbitrary rejections. Liberal regimes prefer this to overt violence—appears technical rather than political.

---

### Resistance and Counter-Power

Power provokes resistance. How do those designated as enemies resist?

**Exit**: Leave the system. Migration, defection, desertion, dropping out. Reduces power's reach. Difficult when borders controlled, but always some manage to escape. Brain drain from authoritarian regimes, refugees fleeing violence, tax havens for capital.

**Voice**: Protest, petition, advocate for change within system. Assumes some responsiveness. Civil rights movements, labor organizing, democratic opposition. Requires minimal openness—impossible in truly totalitarian regimes.

**Loyalty**: Acquiesce publicly while maintaining private resistance. "Weapons of the weak" (Scott)—foot-dragging, dissimulation, hidden transcripts. Peasants pretend submission while sabotaging from within. *(Scott, Weapons of the Weak)*

**Revolution**: Violent overthrow of system. When exit blocked and voice ineffective, oppressed may attempt to seize power. French Revolution, October Revolution, anti-colonial revolutions, slave rebellions. High risk but potentially transformative.

**Refusal**: Simply refuse to participate. Tax resistance, draft resistance, general strike, non-cooperation. Disrupts system by withdrawing labor/compliance. Ghandi's satyagraha, civil disobedience movements. *(Butler, "Bodies in Alliance")*

**Appropriation**: Seize and repurpose tools of power. Guerrilla warfare, hacking, culture jamming. Turn enemy's weapons against them. Weak use strong's own force through asymmetric strategies. *(Certeau, Practice of Everyday Life)*

**Consciousness-raising**: Develop critical awareness of oppression. Feminist consciousness-raising groups, Freirean critical pedagogy, Black Power, Dalit movements. Transform victims into agents who recognize and name their enemies. *(Freire, Pedagogy of the Oppressed)*

**Coalition-building**: Unite disparate groups against common enemy. "enemy of my enemy" logic. Broad fronts against fascism, rainbow coalitions, anti-globalization movements. Difficult to maintain—different groups have different interests.

---

### Transformation of Enmity: From Enemies to Non-Enemies

Under what conditions can friend-enemy distinctions be transcended?

**1. Reconciliation**

After conflict, former enemies become at least non-enemies if not friends. Requires:
- Acknowledgment of harms done by both sides
- Apologies and accountability
- Restitution/reparations where possible
- Shared future vision
- Institutional changes preventing recurrence

Examples: Post-apartheid South Africa (Truth and Reconciliation Commission), post-WWII Franco-German rapprochement, Northern Ireland Good Friday Agreement.

Limits: Requires roughly equal power. Victor-vanquished dynamic precludes genuine reconciliation. Must have common ground for moving forward.

**2. Integration into Shared Framework**

Transform enemies into adversaries within rules. Mouffe's agonistic democracy. Political opponents compete within democratic institutions rather than seeking to destroy each other.

Requirements:
- Agreement on fundamental rules
- Acceptance of electoral outcomes
- Restraint in tactics
- Recognition of legitimate plurality

Fragile: Requires all sides to value system more than particular outcomes. Economic crisis or existential threats can break down into antagonism.

**3. Depoliticization**

Remove intensity from distinction so it no longer structures friend-enemy. Wars of Religion ended not by religious unity but by making religion politically irrelevant. Peace of Westphalia.

Can work for some distinctions (religion in modern West) but not others (race, class still structure friend-enemy despite liberal "color-blindness").

Problem: What is depoliticized can be repoliticized. White Christian nationalism repoliticizes religion. Populism repoliticizes what liberalism tried to technocratize.

**4. Common Enemy**

Unite against shared threat. Supranational solidarity against common enemy. Anti-fascist Popular Front united communists, socialists, liberals against fascism. Climate crisis could potentially unite humanity against shared threat.

Schmitt's prediction: Common enemy just creates new friend-enemy at higher level. Defeating Nazis led to Cold War. Defeating al-Qaeda led to ISIS. Always new enemies.

**5. Mutual Exhaustion**

After protracted conflict, neither side can continue. Stalemate leads to settlement. WWI trenches, Korea, often civil wars.

Problem: Doesn't resolve underlying issues. Enmity persists in suspended form. Can reignite when power balance shifts.

**6. Structural Transformation**

Change social structures creating enmity. Abolish classes (Marx), end patriarchy (feminism), decolonize (anti-imperialism). If enmity is structural, must transform structures.

Problem: How to achieve transformation without violence? Revolutionary transformation typically requires identifying and overcoming enemies of transformation (counter-revolution). The revolutionaries' paradox.

**7. Universalization**

Expand circle of moral concern to include former enemies as equal members of humanity. Cosmopolitanism, human rights discourse.

Schmitt's critique: Universalism conceals particular interests. "Humanity" is weapon against those excluded from it. "Crimes against humanity" criminalize enemies absolutely.

But: Does provide language for limiting violence even toward enemies. War crimes doctrine, Geneva Conventions, human rights protections—all constrain treatment of enemies.

---

## Spatial and Territorial Dimensions of Friend-Enemy

Geography and space structure enmity in crucial ways:

### The Politics of Boundaries

Borders don't just mark where one state ends and another begins—they embody friend-enemy distinctions materialized in space:

**Natural vs. artificial borders**: "Natural" borders (rivers, mountains) seem less arbitrary but still politically constructed. Rhine as Franco-German border fought over for centuries. "Natural" borders often most contested because both sides can claim them.

**Border walls**: Berlin Wall, Israeli West Bank barrier, US-Mexico border wall all physically manifest enmity. Walls create "us" vs. "them" visible in landscape. Must be actively maintained through violence—crossers shot, detained, repelled.

**Buffer zones and demilitarized zones**: Korean DMZ, Cyprus Green Line create spatial manifestation of frozen enmity. Liminal zones that are neither here nor there. Enmity spatialized as empty space between enemies.

**Enclaves and exclaves**: Territorial discontinuity creates enemies within friends or friends within enemies. Creates instability—Kosovo, Kaliningrad, Gibraltar, Hong Kong. Spatial anomaly typically reflects unresolved friend-enemy conflict.

**Militarized borders**: Heavy military presence at borders between enemies. India-Pakistan Line of Control most militarized border in world. Indo-China border, Korean border, many post-Soviet borders. Concentration of violence-capacity at friend-enemy boundary.

---

### Territorial Conquest and Lebensraum

Nazi concept of Lebensraum (living space) reveals spatial logic of enmity:

Enemy peoples occupy space that "we" need. Must be displaced/eliminated to make room for us. Links enmity to territory in zero-sum way. Manifest Destiny, settler colonialism, Israeli settlement expansion, Rwandan Hutu justifications for eliminating Tutsi all express this logic.

Schmitt's Großraum theory attempts to legitimize territorial expansion by powerful states. Each great power entitled to sphere of influence/control. Monroe Doctrine for everyone. But whose Großraum? Conflicts between competing imperialisms. Nazi Großraum clashed with Soviet, both clashed with American.

---

### Cities, Architecture, and the Built Environment

Urban space structures friend-enemy:

**Segregation**: Residential segregation by race (US, South Africa), religion (Belfast, Beirut), class (Paris suburbs, Latin American favelas) spatially separates friends from enemies. Ghettos, townships, camps confine enemy populations.

**Checkpoints and green zones**: Iraq Green Zone, Israeli checkpoints create protected space for friends, controlled access denying enemies. Architecture of occupation.

**Gated communities**: Wealthy sequester themselves from dangerous Others. Literal walls separating rich friends from poor enemies. Privatized security enforcing boundaries.

**Surveillance architecture**: Panopticon design, CCTV coverage, "defensible space" architecture all designed to make enemies visible and controllable. *(Foucault, Discipline and Punish; Davis, City of Quartz)*

**Hostile architecture**: Benches with armrests preventing homeless from sleeping, spikes under bridges, sounds deterring youth. Architecture weaponized against unwanted (enemy) populations.

**Borders within cities**: "Wrong neighborhood" for certain people. Segregated by informal enforcement—violence or threat of violence keeps enemies out. Urban territoriality reproduces friend-enemy at neighborhood scale.

---

## The Phenomenology of Enmity: Lived Experience

Beyond structural analysis, how does enmity feel? What is subjective experience of being enemy or having enemies?

### The View from Enmity

**Being designated enemy**:

Experience of being marked for exclusion, persecution, elimination. Hypervisibility—constantly noticed, scrutinized, suspected. Yet simultaneously invisibilization—not recognized as full human, reduced to category. *(Du Bois, "double consciousness"; Fanon, "lived experience of the Black man")*

**Paranoia**: Never safe. Must always be vigilant. Any interaction with friends/rulers potentially dangerous. Develop hyper-sensitivity to threat. PTSD-like symptoms from living under threat.

**Internalization**: May internalize enemy designation. Come to believe you deserve mistreatment. Colonized mind (Fanon), abused spouse, prisoner who accepts guilt. Most insidious form of power—enemy polices themselves.

**Rage and ressentiment**: Burning anger at injustice combined with inability to effectively resist. Nietzsche's ressentiment—impotent rage that curdles into resentment and desire for revenge. Can motivate resistance but can also be paralyzing or self-destructive.

**Defiance**: Refusing enemy designation, asserting full humanity despite efforts to deny it. "I am a man!" (Memphis sanitation workers, 1968). Black pride, gay pride, ethnic nationalism of oppressed groups all refuse enemy status.

**Exhaustion**: Constant vigilance, stress of enemy status wears people down. "Tired of being tired." Can't sustain permanent emergency. May lead to resignation, apathy, submission.

**Solidarity with co-enemies**: Finding community with those who share enemy status. Oppression creates bonds. But also competition among oppressed for scarce scraps thrown by oppressors.

---

### Having Enemies

**Self-righteousness**: Conviction of own moral superiority. We are good, they are evil. Provides meaning and purpose—we are the good guys fighting bad guys. Clarifies world into simple binary.

**Fear and anxiety**: Enemies threaten us. Must be vigilant. They could attack at any moment. Leads to security theater, militarization, authoritarian acceptance. "If you see something, say something."

**Guilt (sometimes)**: Awareness that enemy status may be unjust, that we benefit from their oppression. Most defend against this through denial or rationalization. But some experience guilt that leads to solidarity with enemies against one's own side.

**Dehumanization**: Psychological mechanism to overcome moral barriers to violence. If enemies are subhuman, harming them less problematic. Must actively maintain—keeps slipping back to recognition of shared humanity. Requires constant propaganda reinforcement.

**Excitement and meaning**: Conflict with enemies provides purpose, clear goals, meaningful action. Soldiers describe war as most meaningful experience despite (because of?) danger and horror. Friend-enemy struggle gives life structure and significance. *(Hedges, War Is a Force That Gives Us Meaning)*

---

## Edge Cases and Ambiguities: When Friend-Enemy Breaks Down

The friend-enemy binary isn't as clean as Schmitt suggests. Many relationships resist classification:

**1. Frenemies**: Friends who are also rivals. Simultaneously cooperating and competing. Great power relations often this way—trade partners who are also military competitors. Can't afford to destroy each other but can't fully trust either.

**2. Neutral parties**: Switzerland, Sweden during WWII. Claim not to be friends or enemies of belligerents. Schmitt says this is impossible—neutrality is itself political choice that antagonizes those who demand you choose sides. But historical neutrality shows it's possible (if militarily defendable).

**3. Hostages and captives**: How to categorize prisoners of war, slaves, colonized populations? Are they enemies (they were fighting us) or friends (now under our control)? Ambiguous status leads to contested treatment. Are they people we're at war with or our own subjects?

**4. Diasporas**: Ethnic/religious groups spread across multiple political communities. Are they loyal to host state or to co-ethnics elsewhere? Permanent suspicion of divided loyalties. Jews as "international," overseas Chinese, Muslim immigrants in West all suspect as potential fifth column.

**5. Traitors and defectors**: Those who cross friend-enemy line. Were they always enemies (infiltrators) or friends who became enemies (traitors)? More hated than born enemies because betrayal worse than honorable opposition. *(Turncoats, quislings, collaborators)*

**6. Allies of convenience**: Strange bedfellows. US allied with Stalin against Hitler, then opposed Stalin in Cold War. Saudi Arabia allies with US despite ideological incompatibility. Not friends but common enemies create temporary alliance. Schmitt's "real enemy" vs. "absolute enemy" distinction—can ally with real enemy against absolute enemy.

**7. Internal dissidents**: Loyal opposition or internal enemies? Democratic theory says legitimate to oppose policies while supporting system. But how much opposition before becomes enemy? Radical movements (communists, fascists, jihadists) claim loyalty to people while rejecting system. Are they legitimate opposition or enemies?

**8. Refugees**: Are they victims fleeing enemies or enemies themselves? Refugee crises generate fierce debates about whether fleeing enemies or actually enemies pretending to be refugees (terrorists among migrants, etc.). Liminality of refugee status—neither clearly enemy nor clearly friend.

---

## Temporal Dynamics: Enemy Histories and Futures

Friend-enemy distinctions evolve over time:

### Historical Memory and Inherited Enmities

Groups inherit enmities from ancestors:

**Long-duration conflicts**: Serb-Croat, Sunni-Shia, Israeli-Arab conflicts stretch across generations. Each generation socialized into inherited enemy designation. Historical grievances keep enmity alive—"Remember 1389!" (Battle of Kosovo), "Never forget!" (Holocaust).

**Chosen trauma**: Collective memory of past victimization by enemies. Armenian genocide, Irish famine, Native American genocide, African American slavery/Jim Crow. Past suffering becomes constitutive of group identity. Can motivate justice-seeking or fuel cycles of revenge.

**Forgetting and moving on**: Sometimes enmity fades as new generations lack lived memory. Franco-German enmity largely overcome (though Brexit and European tensions show it can resurface). Post-WWII reconciliation required conscious effort to move beyond inherited enmity.

**Instrumentalization of history**: Political entrepreneurs mobilize historical enmities for contemporary purposes. Milosevic weaponized Battle of Kosovo memory to mobilize Serbian nationalism. Historical memory isn't just remembered but actively constructed and deployed.

---

### The Future of Enmity

Speculating about future friend-enemy formations:

**Transhumanism and human enhancement**: If some humans radically enhanced through technology, could create new friend-enemy between "naturals" and "posthumans." Gattaca-style genetic discrimination. (*Habermas, Fukuyama both warn of this)*

**Artificial intelligence**: If AGI emerges, humans vs. AI could become species-level friend-enemy. Or AI could make human friend-enemy distinctions obsolete by surpassing us entirely. Or humans might divide over AI (Luddites vs. accelerationists).

**Space colonization**: If humanity expands to other planets, could Earth vs. Mars conflicts emerge? Independence movements on colonies? Or species-unity against alien threats?

**Climate catastrophe**: Severe climate change could create resource wars, climate refugee crises, eco-fascist movements. Or could unite humanity against common threat. Likely both—some cooperation, many new enmities.

**Pandemic and bioweapon**: COVID showed how disease creates friend-enemy (China blamed, Asian hate crimes, anti-vaxx vs. pro-vaxx). Future more lethal pandemics could intensify. Bioweapons could make invisible enemies ubiquitous.

**Virtual/cyber**: If people spend most time in virtual worlds, could digital identities become more salient than physical? Online harassment, doxxing, swatting already create cyber-enemies with real-world consequences. Crypto wars between states and decentralized networks.

---

## PART II: CONCRETE POWER DYNAMICS AND REAL CONSEQUENCES

## The Economic Domain: Capitalist Power and Death by Market Forces

### The Power to Cause Death Through Poverty

The most invisible yet pervasive form of enemy-designation in modern capitalism: those whose death enriches you are not recognized as enemies you've killed, but as "market casualties" or "inevitable inefficiencies."

**The structural violence of poverty**:

When a pharmaceutical company prices insulin such that diabetics cannot afford it and die, has the company killed them? Liberal capitalism says no—the company merely set a price; the diabetics "failed to afford" treatment. This linguistic move obscures friend-enemy: the diabetic is treated as neutral market participant who happened to lose, not as enemy whose death enriches shareholders.

**Actual mechanism**:
- Company patents life-saving drug
- Sets price beyond reach of poor
- Poor die preventable deaths
- Company profits increase
- Shareholders benefit from deaths
- System treats this as neutral "price discovery"

**Friend-enemy translation**: 
- Friends = shareholders whose wealth increases
- Enemies = poor whose deaths increase that wealth
- But enmity is hidden through: "It's just business," "fiduciary duty to shareholders," "market efficiency"

**Real consequences**:
- ~45,000 annual deaths in US from lack of health insurance (Harvard/Cambridge study)
- Deaths are not random—systematically fall on poor, minorities, those without power
- These deaths directly benefit those with power (lower labor costs, higher profits, cheaper goods for wealthy)
- System prevents recognizing this as friend-enemy conflict by framing as "personal responsibility," "market outcomes," "natural consequences"

### Lawfare: Legal Power as Slow-Motion Violence

The law appears neutral but operates as weapon wielded by those who can afford it:

**The insurance clause example**:

Corporation includes mandatory arbitration clause in contract. Employee signs (lacks power to negotiate). Employee suffers harm from corporate negligence. Arbitration:
- Costs $10,000+ upfront
- Corporation can afford; employee cannot
- Employee cannot sue
- Corporation escapes accountability
- Employee bears full cost of harm

**Friend-enemy analysis**:
- Corporation used legal power to pre-emptively disarm potential enemy (harmed employee)
- Legal system enforces this disarmament
- Those who can afford lawyers are friends; those who cannot are enemies
- But framed as "contract law," "freedom of contract," "mutual agreement"

**Real consequences**:
- 60+ million Americans bound by forced arbitration clauses
- Cannot sue employers for wage theft, discrimination, harassment
- Corporate wrongdoing goes unpunished
- Victims bear full costs
- This is legalized predation, but friend-enemy designation is obscured

**The poverty-criminal pipeline**:

Cannot afford bail → sit in jail → lose job → cannot pay rent → become homeless → criminalized for homelessness → incarcerated → cycle repeats.

Each step involves power:
- Bail system: Criminalizes poverty (poor are enemies who must be controlled)
- Employer firing: Labor discipline (expendable enemies)
- Landlord eviction: Property rights trump survival (enemies who don't pay)
- Homeless criminalization: Space control (enemies who don't belong)
- Incarceration: Warehousing and exploiting enemies (prison labor)

**Real consequence**: ~500,000 people incarcerated pre-trial in US because too poor for bail. Not convicted of crimes—jailed for being poor. Friend-enemy: Those with money are friends (released); those without are enemies (caged).

### Housing: The Power to Make People Homeless

**Landlord power**:

Landlord owns multiple properties. Sets rents at market-clearing prices. Tenant cannot afford rent. Tenant becomes homeless. Tenant dies of exposure.

**Liberal framing**: Landlord merely exercised property rights. Tenant's homelessness and death are "unfortunate" but landlord didn't cause them—tenant just couldn't afford housing.

**Friend-enemy reality**:
- Landlord's profit requires tenant's deprivation
- Vacant properties exist while people sleep outside
- Property rights prioritize landlord's profit over tenant's survival
- Homeless person is enemy to be removed (hostile architecture, sweeps, criminalization)
- But enmity is hidden: "It's their property," "housing is a commodity," "incentives"

**Real consequences**:
- ~600,000 homeless in US on any given night
- ~700 deaths per year from exposure in LA County alone
- Millions of vacant properties simultaneously
- These deaths are not accidental—they result from power decisions about who gets to exist where
- Landlords, developers, property owners are friends; homeless are enemies to be eliminated from space

### Employment: The Power of Firing

**The terror of unemployment**:

In wage-labor system, employer has power to deprive you of livelihood. This creates disciplinary power:

- Employer can fire you → you cannot afford food/housing
- Therefore you submit to employer demands
- Work unpaid overtime, accept harassment, don't complain about violations
- Fear of unemployment makes you docile

**Friend-enemy**: 
- Employer is your friend only as long as you remain useful
- Moment you're more expensive than replacement, you become enemy to be eliminated
- "Layoffs," "restructuring," "right-sizing" are euphemisms for "we're eliminating enemies (expensive workers) to benefit friends (shareholders)"

**Real consequences**:
- Lose job → lose health insurance → cannot afford medical care → die of preventable disease
- This causal chain makes employer's firing decision a potential death sentence
- But legal/social system refuses to recognize this as violence
- "Employment at will" doctrine: employer can fire for any reason or no reason
- Your survival depends on remaining useful to those with power over you

**Wage theft**:

Employers steal ~$15 billion/year from workers through various mechanisms:
- Off-the-clock work
- Misclassifying as contractors
- Not paying overtime
- Taking tips
- Minimum wage violations

This theft exceeds all other forms of theft (burglary, robbery, auto theft) COMBINED.

**Friend-enemy**: 
- Workers are enemies to be exploited (extract maximum labor, pay minimum wage)
- System protects employers (weak enforcement, captured regulators, forced arbitration)
- Workers cannot effectively fight back (poverty, fear of retaliation, lack of organization)

**Real consequences**:
- Workers lose money they're legally owed
- Often cannot afford necessities
- Some become homeless, suffer health problems, die
- Employers benefit from this theft
- System treats it as civil dispute, not the systematic predation it is

### Medical System: The Power to Deny Care

**Insurance company power to kill**:

Insurance company denies coverage for treatment. Patient cannot afford treatment out-of-pocket. Patient dies.

Liberal framing: Insurance company was following policy. Patient's death is unfortunate but company didn't kill them—disease did.

**Friend-enemy reality**:
- Insurance company profited by denying care
- Patient died so company could profit
- Shareholder wealth increased because patient died
- Medical professionals wanted to treat; insurance company prevented treatment
- This is killing for profit, but hidden through bureaucratic language

**Real mechanisms**:
- Prior authorization (delays = denials)
- Narrow networks (make necessary care "out of network")
- High deductibles (ensure people can't afford care even with insurance)
- Lifetime caps (cut off care when it gets expensive)
- Exclusions for "pre-existing conditions"
- Formularies that exclude necessary medications

**Real consequences**:
- ~68,000 annual preventable deaths due to lack of adequate insurance (Lancet study)
- Each death benefits insurance company (didn't pay for care)
- Insurance executives earn millions while patients die
- System treats this as acceptable business practice

### Debt: The Power to Bind Through Obligation

**How debt creates enemies**:

Debtor owes creditor money. Creditor has legal power to:
- Garnish wages
- Seize property
- Destroy credit score (prevent future housing, employment, credit)
- Force into bankruptcy
- Have police enforce collection

This is violence, but legal violence. State's monopoly on violence exercised on behalf of creditors against debtors.

**Medical debt**:

Suffer medical emergency → receive necessary care → cannot afford bill → hospital sues → wages garnished → cannot afford rent → become homeless.

Friend-enemy: Sick person is enemy whose misfortune must be exploited. Hospital, collection agency, creditors are friends (protected by law). Debtor is enemy (coerced through state violence).

**Student debt**:

Need education to survive economically → forced to take debt → debt cannot be discharged in bankruptcy → enslaved to creditors for decades → cannot buy house, start family, start business → entire life shaped by debt burden.

**Real consequences**:
- ~43 million Americans in student debt (average ~$30k)
- Monthly payments prevent asset accumulation
- Creates permanent underclass who can never escape debt
- Creditors (often federal government) profit from this bondage
- Young people's life choices constrained by debt burden

**Payday loans and predatory lending**:

Need money to survive → cannot access normal credit → forced to payday lender → 400% APR → cannot repay → roll over loan → permanent debt trap → eventually lose everything.

Friend-enemy: Lender is predator; borrower is prey. But system treats this as "freely chosen contract" between equal parties. Ignores massive power asymmetry.

### Food: The Power to Cause Starvation

**Agricultural capitalism**:

~690 million people are undernourished globally (2019 UN data). This is not because food doesn't exist—we produce enough food to feed 10 billion people. People starve because they cannot afford food.

**Friend-enemy structure**:
- Those who control food (agribusiness, distributors, retailers) are friends
- Those who cannot afford food are enemies whose deaths are acceptable costs
- Food destroyed to maintain prices while people starve
- This is intentional violence but framed as "market efficiency"

**Real mechanisms**:
- Food commodification: Only accessible through purchase
- Agricultural subsidies: Support wealthy farmers, agribusiness
- Crop destruction: Maintain price levels
- Land concentration: Peasants dispossessed, cannot grow own food
- Cash crops over food crops: Export crops for profit vs. feeding locals

**Real consequences**:
- ~9 million die annually from hunger-related causes
- Most could be prevented if food were distributed based on need vs. ability to pay
- But this would reduce profits for food industry
- Deaths are not accidental—they're structural feature of system prioritizing profit over survival

### Climate Capitalism: The Power to Destroy Habitability

**Fossil capital as death-dealing**:

Fossil fuel companies have known since 1970s that their products would cause catastrophic climate change. Continued extraction anyway. Funded climate denial. Blocked climate action.

**Friend-enemy**:
- Fossil fuel executives, shareholders = friends benefiting from extraction
- Future generations whose world is destroyed = enemies (literally future people treated as enemies worth sacrificing for present profit)
- Island nations being submerged = enemies worth destroying
- Climate refugees = enemies to be repelled at borders

**Real consequences**:
- ~5 million annual deaths attributable to fossil fuel air pollution (Harvard study)
- Hundreds of millions of future climate refugees
- Potential collapse of civilization
- This is mass murder for profit, but treated as "energy policy" and "economic growth"

**The carbon asymmetry**:

Top 10% of emitters produce ~50% of emissions. Bottom 50% produce ~10% of emissions. But climate consequences fall disproportionately on those who contributed least:
- Small island nations drowning
- Sub-Saharan Africa experiencing extreme drought
- Bangladesh experiencing flooding
- Global South bearing costs of Global North's consumption

Friend-enemy: Rich who caused problem are friends (protected). Poor who suffer consequences are enemies (expendable).

### Financial Capitalism: The Power to Crash Economies

**The 2008 financial crisis**:

Banks engaged in fraudulent lending → created housing bubble → bubble burst → millions lost homes → banks bailed out → no bankers prosecuted → same people remain in power.

**Friend-enemy**:
- Bankers, financial executives = friends (bailed out, protected)
- Homeowners, workers = enemies (lost homes, jobs, savings)
- Profits privatized, losses socialized
- Those who caused crisis were friends (saved); those who suffered were enemies (left to drown)

**Real consequences**:
- 10 million Americans lost homes to foreclosure
- 8.7 million jobs lost
- $19.2 trillion in household wealth destroyed
- Meanwhile, bankers received billions in bonuses
- No accountability for those who caused crisis
- Many of those foreclosed upon died (suicide, stress, health impacts)

**Austerity as class warfare**:

After crisis caused by financial sector, governments imposed austerity on working class:
- Cut social services
- Reduce pensions
- Privatize public goods
- While maintaining bailouts and tax cuts for wealthy

Friend-enemy: Financial crisis made naked the class enmity. Rich demanded (and received) bailouts. Poor were enemies who must suffer to pay for rich's mistakes.

### Intellectual Property: The Power to Monopolize Knowledge

**Patent power**:

Company develops drug using publicly-funded research → patents drug → charges $100,000/year → poor countries cannot afford → millions die preventable deaths → company maintains monopoly.

**COVID vaccine example**:

Pharmaceutical companies refused to waive vaccine patents during pandemic. Result:
- Wealthy countries vaccinated populations
- Poor countries couldn't access vaccines
- Millions died preventable deaths
- Companies made record profits

Friend-enemy: Those who can afford vaccines are friends (protected). Those who cannot are enemies (expendable). Market-based distribution of life-saving technology ensures the poor die.

**Real consequences**:
- Billions without access to patented medicines
- Companies profit from monopoly pricing
- Deaths are not incidental but structural feature of IP regime
- Knowledge that could save lives is artificially restricted to maximize profit

### Data Capitalism: The Power of Surveillance

**Platform power**:

Tech companies collect massive data on users. Use data to:
- Manipulate behavior
- Predict and prevent resistance
- Sell to highest bidder (including oppressive governments)
- Create addictive products
- Shape political outcomes

**Friend-enemy**:
- Users are not customers but products being sold
- Your data is extracted without meaningful compensation
- You are enemy to be harvested
- Company shareholders are friends benefiting from your exploitation

**Real consequences**:
- Cambridge Analytica scandal: Data used to manipulate elections
- Genocide in Myanmar: Facebook algorithm amplified hate speech
- Mental health epidemic: Addictive design harms users
- Surveillance capitalism: Totalitarian knowledge asymmetry
- Your behavior predicted and shaped by those you cannot see or resist

### Carceral System: The Power of Imprisonment

**Mass incarceration as enemy warehousing**:

US has 5% of world population but 25% of world's prisoners. This is not because Americans are more criminal—it's because incarceration is profitable and politically useful.

**Prison-industrial complex**:

Private prisons profit from incarceration. Prison labor provides cheap labor for corporations. Police unions defend mass incarceration for job security. Politicians campaign on being "tough on crime."

**Friend-enemy**:
- Prisoners are enemies—literally stripped of rights, forced to work, subjected to violence
- Prison corporations, guards unions, politicians are friends benefiting from mass incarceration
- Predominantly Black and poor people incarcerated
- Literally marking certain populations as enemies to be caged

**Real consequences**:
- 2.3 million incarcerated in US
- ~5 million more on probation/parole
- Prison labor pays cents per hour (slavery by another name)
- Families destroyed
- Communities devastated
- Former prisoners unable to vote, get jobs, access housing
- Creates permanent underclass of enemies

### Immigration: The Power of Borders

**Border violence**:

US-Mexico border: Migrants die in desert crossing. Deaths are not accidents—they're result of policy deliberately funneling migrants into deadly terrain.

**Friend-enemy**:
- Migrants are enemies to be repelled, detained, expelled, killed if necessary
- Citizens are friends whose comfort requires excluding enemies
- Deaths are not regrettable side effects but intended consequences of deterrence policy

**Real consequences**:
- ~7,000+ migrant deaths at US-Mexico border since 2014 (known deaths; real number higher)
- Thousands more die in Mediterranean trying to reach Europe
- Detention camps where migrants held in cages
- Family separation as policy
- Deliberate cruelty as deterrence
- These are not unfortunate outcomes but intentional violence against designated enemies

**Economic migration**:

Why do people migrate? Often because:
- Developed countries' policies destroyed their economies
- Climate change (caused by developed countries) destroyed their livelihoods
- Wars (often supported by developed countries) destroyed their homes

Then developed countries treat these migrants as enemies and violently exclude them.

Friend-enemy: We create conditions forcing migration, then treat those fleeing as enemies. This is structural violence and hypocrisy combined.

---

## PART III: IDENTIFYING FRIENDS AND ENEMIES IN PRACTICE

### How to Know Who Your Enemies Actually Are

The liberal-capitalist system obscures friend-enemy relations. Here's how to identify who actually benefits from your harm:

**Follow the material benefits**:

When something bad happens to you, ask: Who profits? Who's material position improves because mine worsened?

**Examples**:

Lost your job → Company's stock price increased (lower labor costs)
- Enemy: Shareholders who benefit from your unemployment
- Friend: Fellow workers who also face this threat

Cannot afford medical care → Insurance company kept your premiums without paying claims
- Enemy: Insurance executives whose bonuses come from denied care
- Friend: Other patients also being denied care

Foreclosed on your home → Bank sold mortgage as security, got bailed out, now owns your home
- Enemy: Financial institutions that profited from your loss
- Friend: Other foreclosed homeowners

**Follow the power asymmetry**:

Who has power over you that you don't have over them?

- Employer can fire you; you cannot fire employer = enemy relationship
- Landlord can evict you; you cannot evict landlord = enemy relationship
- Police can arrest you; you cannot arrest police = enemy relationship
- Creditor can garnish wages; you cannot garnish creditor's = enemy relationship

These asymmetries reveal who can harm you with impunity. Those with unilateral power over you are potential enemies—whether they exercise that power depends on whether your interests align.

**Follow the structural position**:

Your position in various hierarchies determines who benefits from your oppression:

Class hierarchy:
- Those above you benefit from extracting value from your labor
- Those below you are often scapegoated for problems caused by those above
- Actual enemies: Those extracting surplus value
- Potential friends: Those in similar position

Racial hierarchy:
- Whiteness provides material benefits even to poor whites
- This divides working class along racial lines
- Actual enemies: System maintaining racial capitalism
- Potential friends: All workers, but white workers must choose solidarity over white supremacy

Gender hierarchy:
- Patriarchy provides material benefits to men
- Divides potential solidarity along gender lines
- Actual enemies: System maintaining gendered oppression
- Potential friends: All oppressed by patriarchy, but men must choose solidarity over patriarchal privilege

**The trick of false enemies**:

Power always tries to redirect your enmity toward false enemies:

Capital directs white workers' enmity toward immigrants rather than capitalists extracting surplus value from all workers.

Men directed to see women as enemies competing for scarce resources, rather than seeing patriarchal capitalism as enemy restricting resources.

Citizens directed to see foreign enemies (terrorism, China, Russia) rather than seeing domestic ruling class as enemy.

Middle class directed to see poor as enemies (welfare queens, lazy takers) rather than seeing rich as enemies (tax avoiders, wealth hoarders).

**How to identify false enemies**:

Ask: Does this supposed enemy actually have power over me? Or are we both relatively powerless, fighting over scraps?

Immigrants "stealing jobs": Immigrants don't control hiring; capitalists do. Capitalists benefit from workers divided along ethnic lines. Immigrants are false enemies; capitalists are real enemies.

Poor people "draining resources": Poor don't control budget priorities; politicians and wealthy do. Rich benefit from middle class resentment directed downward rather than upward. Poor are false enemies; rich are real enemies.

Other countries "threatening us": Foreign workers don't control your working conditions; your employer does. Military-industrial complex benefits from permanent foreign threats justifying massive spending. Foreign civilians are false enemies; war-profiteers are real enemies.

### The Friend-Enemy Sorting Algorithm

For any given actor, determine their relationship to you:

**Step 1**: Do they have significant power over you?
- Yes → Potential enemy (proceed to Step 2)
- No → Potential friend or irrelevant (proceed to Step 3)

**Step 2**: Does their material interest conflict with yours?
- Yes → Enemy (they benefit from your harm)
- No → Possibly friend, but maintain vigilance (power corrupts)

**Step 3**: Could you ally with them against mutual enemies?
- Yes → Potential friend (build solidarity)
- No → Irrelevant (no basis for friendship or enmity)

**Step 4**: Have they actually harmed you or people like you?
- Yes → Active enemy (respond accordingly)
- No → Latent enemy or not-yet-friend (watch carefully)

**Examples applying this algorithm**:

**Your Boss**:
- Step 1: Significant power? YES (can fire you, set wages, determine conditions)
- Step 2: Conflicting interest? YES (profits from paying you less, extracting more work)
- Conclusion: ENEMY (may be polite, even "nice," but structural enemy)

**Fellow Worker**:
- Step 1: Significant power? NO (same position as you)
- Step 3: Mutual enemies? YES (both exploited by same boss)
- Conclusion: POTENTIAL FRIEND (if solidarity develops)

**Undocumented Immigrant Worker**:
- Step 1: Significant power? NO (less power than you)
- Step 3: Mutual enemies? YES (both exploited by capitalist class)
- Conclusion: POTENTIAL FRIEND (capital wants you to see as enemy)

**CEO of Your Company**:
- Step 1: Significant power? YES (controls your employment)
- Step 2: Conflicting interest? YES (wealth grows from surplus value extracted from your labor)
- Step 4: Actual harm? YES (pays you less than value you create)
- Conclusion: ACTIVE ENEMY (benefits daily from exploiting you)

**Police Officer**:
- Step 1: Significant power? YES (can arrest, use violence, kill with near-impunity)
- Step 2: Conflicting interest? DEPENDS (if you're poor/minority, YES; if wealthy/white, less so)
- Conclusion: ENEMY for the oppressed; FRIEND for the propertied

### The Complexity: When Enemies Must Appear as Friends

Modern power requires masking enmity:

**Human Resources as enemy posing as friend**:

HR departments exist to protect company from employees, but present themselves as employee advocates. When you go to HR with problem:
- They document everything you say
- Use it against you if you later sue
- Protect company, not you

But they smile, call you by first name, pretend to care. Enemy wearing friendly mask.

**Managers as "coaches"**:

Modern management speaks language of empowerment, growth, teamwork. But structural relationship unchanged:
- Manager extracts surplus value
- Manager can fire you
- Manager's advancement depends on squeezing more from workers

Enemy using therapeutic language to obscure enmity.

**"Socially responsible" corporations**:

Company claims to care about environment, workers, social justice. Meanwhile:
- Exploits workers
- Pollutes environment
- Lobbies against regulation
- Extracts maximum profit

Enemy using moral language to obscure enmity while continuing to harm.

### The Tragedy of Intersectional Enemies

Same person can be enemy in one dimension, friend in another:

**White working-class man**:
- Class: Potential friend (exploited by capital)
- Race: Structural enemy (benefits from white supremacy, often attacks solidarity with workers of color)
- Gender: Structural enemy (benefits from patriarchy, often attacks women workers)

How to relate? Depends on whether he chooses solidarity (friend) or privilege (enemy).

**Professional-class woman of color**:
- Gender: Friend (oppressed by patriarchy)
- Race: Friend (oppressed by white supremacy)
- Class: Enemy (benefits from exploitation of working class)

How to relate? Depends on whether she prioritizes identity solidarity or class interest.

This is why intersectional analysis is necessary but also why politics is so complicated. Same person can be enemy and friend simultaneously in different dimensions of power.

### The Ultimate Question: Who Can Kill You With Impunity?

This is the deepest way to identify enemies: Who has power to cause your death without consequence?

**Employer**: Can fire you → you lose healthcare → you die of treatable illness
- Consequence to employer: None (legal and normal)
- Conclusion: Enemy with power to kill indirectly

**Landlord**: Can evict you → you become homeless → you die of exposure
- Consequence to landlord: None (exercising property rights)
- Conclusion: Enemy with power to kill indirectly

**Police**: Can shoot you → you die
- Consequence to police: Qualified immunity, police unions protect, rarely prosecuted
- Conclusion: Enemy with power to kill directly

**Insurance company**: Can deny coverage → you cannot afford treatment → you die
- Consequence to company: None (following policy, maximizing profit)
- Conclusion: Enemy with power to kill indirectly

**State**: Can imprison you → you die in prison (medical neglect, violence, etc.)
- Consequence to state: None (prisoners dying is routine)
- Conclusion: Enemy with power to kill directly

**Comparison**:

If you killed any of these actors, you would face severe consequences (prison, execution). They can kill you with impunity. This asymmetry reveals true enemy relationships.

The liberal-capitalist system obscures this by:
- Calling direct killing "use of force" when state does it
- Calling indirect killing "market outcomes" when capital does it
- Treating your resistance as illegitimate violence
- Treating their violence as legitimate authority or neutral process

---

## PART IV: DOMAINS OF POWER - COMPREHENSIVE MAPPING

### Educational Power: The Power to Shape Minds

**The school-to-prison pipeline**:

Poor students, especially Black and Latino boys, disproportionately:
- Suspended for minor infractions
- Labeled as "behavioral problems"
- Pushed out of school
- Funneled into criminal justice system

Meanwhile, rich students:
- Given "second chances"
- Behavioral problems treated as needing support
- Connections ensure college admission despite mediocrity
- Pipeline to power, not prison

**Friend-enemy**:
- Rich students are friends (future leaders)
- Poor students are enemies (future prisoners)
- School system sorts children into friends and enemies early

**Real consequences**:
- Black students 3-4x more likely to be suspended
- School suspension predicts later incarceration
- Educational attainment determines lifetime earnings
- System reproduces class/race hierarchy across generations

**Debt peonage through student loans**:

Make higher education necessary for middle-class life → make it unaffordable → force students into debt → enslave graduates to creditors for decades.

Friend-enemy: Creditors benefit; debtors suffer. But framed as "investment in yourself" rather than structural exploitation.

### Medical Power: The Power Over Life and Death

**The medical caste system**:

Quality of medical care depends on:
- Insurance quality (which depends on employment)
- Geographic location (medical deserts in poor areas)
- Race (Black patients systematically undertreated)
- Ability to navigate bureaucracy

This creates tiers:
- Tier 1: Wealthy (concierge medicine, immediate care, best doctors)
- Tier 2: Insured middle-class (adequate care with hoops to jump through)
- Tier 3: Medicaid (long waits, limited options, stigma)
- Tier 4: Uninsured (emergency rooms only, medical bankruptcy)

**Friend-enemy structure**:
- Those in higher tiers are friends (deserving of care)
- Those in lower tiers are enemies (undeserving, draining resources)
- System ensures the poor die earlier and suffer more

**Real consequences**:
- ~74,000 annual preventable deaths due to inadequate healthcare access
- Life expectancy varies by >20 years between richest and poorest neighborhoods
- Black Americans have higher mortality for nearly every cause
- These aren't accidents—they're structural violence

### Reproductive Power: The Power Over Reproduction

**Forced birth as control**:

Restrict abortion → force women to carry unwanted pregnancies → trap women in poverty, abusive relationships, health problems → reduce women's economic and political power.

**Friend-enemy**:
- Women who can control reproduction are friends (can participate in public life)
- Women forced to bear children are enemies (relegated to domestic sphere, impoverished)
- Men benefit from women's reproductive servitude
- Capital benefits from captive low-wage female labor

**Real consequences**:
- Abortion restrictions disproportionately harm poor women
- Rich women can always access abortion (travel, pay doctors)
- Forced pregnancy is violence
- Maternal mortality in US highest in developed world (especially for Black women)

**Sterilization as genocide**:

Conversely, forced sterilization used against women deemed "unfit":
- Indigenous women
- Women with disabilities
- Poor women
- Black women
- Incarcerated women

Friend-enemy: Dominant group decides who deserves to reproduce. "Undesirable" populations are enemies whose reproduction must be prevented.

### Linguistic Power: The Power to Name

**Who gets to define terms**:

Power determines what counts as:
- "Terrorism" vs. "legitimate resistance"
- "Riot" vs. "protest" vs. "uprising"
- "Looting" vs. "wealth accumulation"
- "Violence" vs. "law enforcement"
- "Aggression" vs. "self-defense"

When powerful do something, it's legitimate. When powerless do same thing, it's criminal.

**Examples**:

Police kill Black man → "Officer-involved shooting" (passive voice, sanitized)
Black man allegedly steals item → "Thug criminals destroying community" (active voice, demonizing)

US bombs foreign country → "Intervention," "bringing democracy," "protecting interests"
Foreign country resists US bombing → "Terrorism," "rogue state," "threat to international order"

Rich person avoids taxes through legal means → "Tax strategy," "smart business"
Poor person receives government benefits → "Welfare queen," "drain on society," "taking your tax dollars"

**Friend-enemy**:
- Friends' actions are legitimized through language
- Enemies' actions are delegitimized through language
- This is power—the ability to make your violence disappear through naming

### Knowledge Power: The Power to Determine Truth

**Expert gatekeeping**:

Who counts as legitimate knower?
- Credentialed experts (mostly wealthy, white, male)
- Peer review controlled by insiders
- Funding determines what gets researched
- Publication access requires institutional affiliation

This excludes:
- Working-class knowledge
- Indigenous knowledge
- Women's knowledge
- Non-Western knowledge

**Friend-enemy**:
- Credentialed experts are friends (legitimate knowers)
- Others are enemies (ignorant, superstitious, need to be educated)
- Power determines whose knowledge counts

**Real consequences**:
- Medical racism: Black patients' pain systematically undertreated (doctors don't believe them)
- Climate denial: Fossil fuel industry manufactured doubt
- Tobacco industry: Delayed recognition of cancer link for decades
- Pharmaceutical industry: Controls research on drug efficacy
- All cases where power distorts knowledge to benefit friends, harm enemies

### Aesthetic Power: The Power to Define Beauty
