**Beauty standards as violence**:

Dominant group's features defined as beautiful:
- White features as beauty standard (skin-lightening industry, rhinoplasty, etc.)
- Thin bodies as beauty standard (eating disorders, fat discrimination)
- Able bodies as beauty standard (ableism)
- Youth as beauty standard (ageism)

**Friend-enemy**:
- Those who meet standards are friends (rewarded with higher status, better treatment)
- Those who don't are enemies (punished through discrimination, mockery, exclusion)

**Real consequences**:
- Fat people paid less, hired less, promoted less, provided worse medical care
- Dark-skinned people discriminated against (colorism)
- Disabled people excluded from public space, employment, relationships
- These standards cause measurable material harm

### Technological Power: The Power of Access and Exclusion

**The digital divide as new form of enmity**:

Modern life requires internet access, smartphones, digital literacy. Those without are excluded from:
- Jobs (applications online only)
- Education (remote learning requires tech)
- Healthcare (telemedicine)
- Government services (moved online)
- Social connection (especially during COVID)

**Friend-enemy**:
- Those with tech access are friends (full participation)
- Those without are enemies (excluded, left behind)
- System treats this as personal failing rather than structural exclusion

**Algorithmic enmity**:

Algorithms decide:
- Who gets hired (resume screening AI)
- Who gets loans (credit scoring)
- Who gets arrested (predictive policing)
- Who gets shown what content (filter bubbles)
- Who gets surveilled (facial recognition)

These algorithms encode existing prejudices:
- Discriminate against minorities (trained on biased data)
- Reinforce existing inequalities
- Operate invisibly (proprietary, no accountability)

**Real consequences**:
- Amazon's resume screening AI discriminated against women
- COMPAS criminal risk algorithm biased against Black defendants
- Facebook's algorithm amplified genocide in Myanmar
- Nextdoor's algorithm enabled racial profiling
- Those designated enemies by algorithms face systematic discrimination

### Temporal Power: The Power Over Time

**Who controls your time?**

Employer controls your time:
- 40+ hours/week at workplace
- Must be available when they need you
- Cannot leave even to use bathroom (Amazon warehouse workers)
- Unpredictable schedules prevent planning life

**Friend-enemy**:
- Employer's time is valuable (billable, respected)
- Worker's time is worthless (must sell it to survive)
- Rich buy back time (hire others to do tasks)
- Poor cannot buy time (work multiple jobs)

**Real consequences**:
- Working-class people have no time for:
  - Political participation
  - Self-education
  - Health maintenance
  - Relationship cultivation
  - Rest and recovery
- This is power—ensuring enemies are too exhausted to resist

**The waiting room as violence**:

Poor people spend enormous time waiting:
- At DMV
- At social services office
- At free clinic
- At parole office
- At unemployment office

This is not accidental. It's disciplinary:
- Your time is worthless
- You must prove you deserve help
- You will be made to suffer for asking
- This discourages seeking help (which is the point)

Rich people never wait. Concierge services, private appointments, jump queues. Their time is respected; yours is not.

### Spatial Power: The Power to Control Movement

**Who can go where?**

Rich:
- Can travel freely (powerful passports)
- Can enter any neighborhood
- Can access any space
- Are welcomed everywhere

Poor:
- Restricted by borders
- Criminalized in rich neighborhoods ("suspicious")
- Excluded from spaces (no loitering, customers only)
- Chased from public space

**Real consequences**:
- Homeless person arrested for sleeping in park
- Rich person with mansion sleeping soundly
- Black teenager followed in store
- White teenager not suspected
- Mexican migrant dies in desert
- American tourist welcomed in Mexico

### Reputational Power: The Power to Destroy or Elevate

**Who can destroy your reputation?**

Powerful can:
- Smear enemies (media access, platforms)
- Destroy careers (blacklisting)
- Ruin through accusation (no due process needed)
- Rehabilitate their own crimes

Powerless:
- Have no platform
- Cannot respond effectively
- Accusations stick permanently
- No mechanism for rehabilitation

**#MeToo example**:

When accusation against powerful man:
- He gets book deal, podcast, rehabilitation tour
- "Innocent until proven guilty" invoked
- Accuser smeared, threatened, harassed

When accusation against powerless person:
- Fired immediately
- Blacklisted
- No second chance
- Presumption of guilt

Friend-enemy: Power determines whose reputation deserves protection.

### Cultural Power: The Power to Define Normal

**Whose culture is "normal"?**

Dominant culture is invisible (unmarked):
- White culture isn't "white culture," it's just "culture"
- Male perspective isn't "male perspective," it's just "perspective"
- Straight relationships aren't "straight relationships," they're just "relationships"
- Christian holidays aren't "Christian holidays," they're just "holidays"

**Friend-enemy**:
- Dominant culture is friends (normal, universal, human)
- Other cultures are enemies (particular, ethnic, other)

**Real consequences**:
- Muslim woman wearing hijab marked as other
- White man in suit unmarked (assumed competent)
- Black cultural expressions pathologized
- White cultural expressions celebrated

---

## PART V: THE CONSEQUENCES - WHAT HAPPENS WHEN YOU MISIDENTIFY

### Misidentifying Enemies: Fighting the Wrong Target

**The cost of attacking false enemies**:

When white workers attack immigrant workers instead of capitalists:
- Immigrants are harmed
- Capitalists benefit (divided working class)
- White workers don't improve their position
- Everyone except capital loses

When men attack feminism instead of patriarchal capitalism:
- Women harmed
- Capitalism benefits (divided resistance)
- Men don't actually improve (still exploited by capital)
- Everyone except capital loses

**The pattern**: Power directs enmity toward false enemies who cannot really harm you, away from real enemies who are actively harming you.

### Misidentifying Friends: Trusting Enemies

**When you mistake enemies for friends**:

Thinking your employer cares about you:
- You don't organize
- You accept exploitation
- You defend their interests against your own
- They benefit; you suffer

Thinking police are your friends:
- You don't resist
- You provide information used against you
- You support policies enabling police violence
- They benefit; you suffer (especially if poor/minority)

Thinking politicians represent you:
- You vote for their interests
- You don't organize outside electoral politics
- You blame yourself when they betray you
- They benefit; you suffer

### The Centrist Fallacy: "There Are No Enemies"

**Liberal denial of enemy relationships**:

Liberalism claims we can all be friends if we just communicate better, find common ground, compromise.

This serves power by:
- Denying real conflicts of interest
- Blaming victims for not being diplomatic enough
- Protecting oppressors from consequences
- Preventing effective resistance

**Real example—slave owners and slaves**:

Can they be friends? Is this a misunderstanding to be resolved through dialogue? NO. Material interests are opposed. Slave owner's wealth requires slave's bondage. This is enemy relationship.

But liberals would say: "Both sides need to communicate better. Find common ground. Compromise."

Compromise between freedom and slavery is continued slavery.

### The Collaborator Problem: Becoming Friend to Your Enemy

**When oppressed side with oppressors**:

Some Jews collaborated with Nazis (Kapos, Judenrat). Some slaves worked as overseers. Some women enforce patriarchy. Some workers defend capitalism.

Why?
- Personal survival (collaborating provides temporary safety)
- Psychological (identifying with power reduces cognitive dissonance)
- Material benefits (collaborators receive small rewards)

But collaboration means:
- Harming your own group
- Strengthening your enemy
- Often not actually ensuring your safety (collaborators often killed anyway)
- Moral corruption

**The calculus**: Collaborate for personal benefit vs. resist for collective liberation?

Liberalism individualizes everything, making collaboration seem rational. But:
- Your personal safety through collaboration depends on others' oppression
- If everyone collaborated, no one would ever be free
- Collaboration reproduces the system harming you

### The Revolutionary Paradox: Creating New Enemies

**When revolution produces new class enemies**:

French Revolution: Overthrow aristocrats → create new enemies (Girondins, then Dantonists, then...) → terror escalates → revolution devours its children.

Soviet Revolution: Overthrow capitalists → create new enemies (kulaks, Trotskyites, wreckers) → endless purges.

**The problem**: Once friend-enemy logic is absolute, there's no mechanism to stop finding new enemies. Revolution requires identifying and destroying enemies. But who decides when all enemies are destroyed?

Answer: Never. Always new enemies. Until everyone is potentially enemy. Totalitarianism.

### The Pacifist Problem: Refusing to Name Enemies

**When you refuse to identify enemies**:

Pacifism claims violence is never justified. But:
- What if someone is violently attacking you?
- What if system is slowly killing you through structural violence?
- What if your children are starving because others hoard?

Refusing to name enemies means:
- Cannot organize effective resistance
- Cannot defend yourself or others
- Allows enemies to continue harming you
- Enables violence through non-resistance

**The paradox**: Absolute pacifism enables violence by refusing to stop it.

Christian "love your enemy":
- Beautiful ideal
- But does it mean not resisting enemy's violence?
- Does it mean allowing them to kill you and others?
- Or does it mean loving them while still stopping their harmful actions?

Depends on interpretation. But if "love your enemy" means "don't stop them from killing you," it's death cult, not ethics.

---

---

## PART VI: LEGAL POWER - THE VIOLENCE OF LAW

### Contracts as Preemptive Disarmament

**The fine print friend-enemy**:

Every contract you sign contains clauses that benefit the more powerful party. You have no power to negotiate these clauses—take it or leave it.

**Employment contracts**:

Standard employment agreement contains:
- Non-compete clause (prevents you from working elsewhere)
- Mandatory arbitration (prevents you from suing)
- At-will employment (can fire you anytime)
- IP assignment (anything you create belongs to company)
- Non-disparagement (cannot criticize company)

You sign because you need the job. Company has team of lawyers. You have none.

**Friend-enemy**:
- Company is enemy pre-emptively disarming you
- You surrender legal rights before conflict even arises
- But framed as "mutual agreement" between equals

**Real consequence**:
- You cannot sue for violations
- You cannot work for competitor even if fired
- You cannot speak publicly about abuses
- You have no recourse when wronged
- Company has complete power; you have none

**Terms of Service as law-making by corporations**:

Facebook, Google, Amazon write their own laws (TOS). You must accept to use services. TOS changes unilaterally—you don't get to negotiate.

These private entities exercise law-making power. Decide:
- What speech is allowed (more restrictive than First Amendment)
- What behavior is permitted
- How disputes are resolved (always in company's favor)
- What data they can collect
- What they can do with your data

Friend-enemy: Corporations are private sovereigns. Users are subjects with no rights except what sovereign grants.

### Intellectual Property as Enclosure of Knowledge

**Patents as monopoly power**:

Patent system grants 20-year monopoly on ideas. Originally meant to incentivize innovation. Actually operates to:
- Concentrate power in large corporations (small inventors cannot afford patent litigation)
- Enable price-gouging (insulin, EpiPen, life-saving drugs)
- Block innovation (patent thickets)
- Transfer public research to private profit

**Real mechanism**:

University researcher (publicly funded) discovers drug → publishes research → pharmaceutical company patents slight variation → charges monopoly prices → original researcher cannot afford drug they discovered.

Friend-enemy:
- Pharmaceutical corporations are friends (protected by IP law)
- Patients needing drugs are enemies (exploited through monopoly)
- Knowledge enclosed, privatized, weaponized

**Copyright as permanent rent-extraction**:

Copyright originally 14 years. Now life of author + 70 years. Disney lobbies to extend copyright every time Mickey Mouse about to enter public domain.

This means:
- Culture stays privately owned
- Must pay rent to access human heritage
- Orphan works (copyright holder unknown) cannot be used legally
- Remix culture criminalized

Friend-enemy: IP holders extract rent from culture. Public are enemies prevented from accessing/using culture.

### Tort Reform as Immunity for Corporate Harm

**Caps on damages**:

Corporation causes harm through negligence. Victims sue. "Tort reform" laws cap damages at arbitrary low amounts.

Example: Medical malpractice caps. Doctor/hospital causes permanent disability through negligence. Victim's lifetime losses = $5 million. Damage cap = $250,000.

Result:
- Victim bears most costs of harm
- Doctor/hospital faces reduced consequences
- Incentive to avoid harm is reduced

Friend-enemy: Corporations protected from full consequences. Victims are enemies who must bear their own suffering.

**Sovereign immunity**:

State causes harm. Victim tries to sue. Sovereign immunity: "The king can do no wrong."

Examples:
- Police brutality: Qualified immunity prevents suits
- Military actions: Government cannot be sued for bombing civilians
- Regulatory failure: State not liable for failing to regulate (even when failure causes deaths)

Friend-enemy: State is friend to itself, enemy to those it harms with impunity.

### Criminal Law as Class Control

**Who gets criminalized?**

Same behavior, different treatment based on power:

**Wage theft by employers** (~$15 billion/year):
- Rarely prosecuted
- Usually civil matter
- Small fines if caught
- No jail time

**Theft by workers** (~$3 billion/year):
- Aggressively prosecuted
- Criminal charges
- Jail time
- Permanent criminal record

**Corporate fraud** (billions in financial crisis):
- No prosecutions of major bankers
- Companies pay fines (no admission of wrongdoing)
- Executives keep jobs and bonuses

**Welfare fraud** (~$100 million/year):
- Aggressively prosecuted
- Harsh penalties
- Public shaming
- Future benefits denied

**Drug crimes**:

Crack cocaine (cheap, used by poor/Black people):
- 100:1 sentencing disparity vs. powder cocaine
- Mandatory minimums
- No rehabilitation
- Life-destroying consequences

Powder cocaine (expensive, used by wealthy/white people):
- Lighter sentences
- Diversion programs
- Rehabilitation options
- Limited consequences

Friend-enemy: Law protects the powerful (friends), punishes the powerless (enemies). Same behavior, opposite treatment based on who you are.

### Family Law as Patriarchal Power

**Custody battles**:

Wealthy parent can afford expensive lawyers. Poor parent cannot. System awards custody based on:
- Who can provide better material conditions (the wealthy parent)
- Who appears more stable (whoever can afford to appear stable)

This means:
- Wealth determines who keeps children
- Poor parents lose children through poverty
- State enables this by prioritizing material conditions over actual parenting

**Divorce as wealth transfer**:

Marriage as economic arrangement. Divorce transfers wealth based on legal maneuvering. Wealthier party can:
- Afford better lawyers
- Hide assets
- Drag out proceedings until other party runs out of money
- Extract favorable settlement through attrition

Friend-enemy: Family law protects property more than people. Wealth determines outcomes.

### Regulatory Capture: When Enemies Write the Rules

**Agencies captured by industries they regulate**:

FDA approves pharmaceuticals → former FDA officials join pharmaceutical companies → companies influence FDA decisions → revolving door ensures agency serves industry, not public.

Same pattern:
- FCC captured by telecom
- SEC captured by finance
- EPA captured by polluters
- USDA captured by agribusiness

**Real consequence**:
- Regulations written to benefit industry
- Public harmed by unsafe products, pollution, financial fraud
- Agencies that should protect public instead serve corporate friends

**Lobbying as legalized bribery**:

Corporations spend billions lobbying:
- Write legislation themselves
- Provide "campaign contributions" (bribes)
- Offer cushy jobs to former legislators
- Threaten to fund opponents of uncooperative legislators

Result: Laws serve corporations, not people.

Friend-enemy: Legislators are friends of corporations (mutual benefit). Public are enemies (harmed by corporate-written laws).

---

## PART VII: INTERNATIONAL POWER ASYMMETRIES

### Imperialism and Neo-Colonialism

**Structural Adjustment Programs as economic warfare**:

Country needs loan → goes to IMF/World Bank → conditionalities imposed:
- Cut social spending
- Privatize public services
- Open markets to foreign capital
- Devalue currency

**Real consequences**:
- Public services collapse
- Poverty increases
- Foreign corporations buy national assets at fire-sale prices
- Debt increases (austerity causes recession, reducing revenue)
- Permanent debt dependency

This is enemy relationship:
- IMF/World Bank serve wealthy countries and international capital
- Debtor countries are enemies to be exploited
- Local populations suffer; foreign investors profit

**Example—Greece**:

Eurozone crisis → Greece needs bailout → Troika (EU/ECB/IMF) imposes austerity:
- Cut pensions 40%
- Cut public sector wages
- Privatize ports, airports, utilities
- Result: GDP contracted 25%, unemployment >25%, suicide rate doubled

Meanwhile: German and French banks (which held Greek debt) were bailed out.

Friend-enemy: Banks were friends (protected). Greek people were enemies (sacrificed).

### Resource Extraction and the Curse

**Oil, minerals, and perpetual exploitation**:

Pattern across Africa, Latin America, Middle East:
- Rich natural resources
- Foreign corporations extract resources
- Tiny elite collaborates
- Vast majority live in poverty
- Environmental devastation
- When locals resist, violence

**Mechanism**:
- Colonial powers/corporations strike deals with local elites
- Elites granted power in exchange for allowing extraction
- Military/police ensure compliance
- Profits exported
- Local population never benefits

**Nigeria example**:

Massive oil wealth. Yet:
- 70% live on <$2/day
- Oil region (Niger Delta) devastated environmentally
- Shell Oil colludes with military to suppress resistance
- Activists executed (Ken Saro-Wiwa)
- Profits go to foreign companies and corrupt elite

Friend-enemy:
- Oil corporations and corrupt elite are friends
- Local population are enemies (impediments to extraction)
- Environmental destruction is acceptable cost

### Debt Imperialism: The New Colonialism

**Debt trap diplomacy**:

Poor country needs infrastructure → wealthy country/company offers loan with strings attached → country cannot repay → creditor seizes assets or extracts policy concessions.

**China's Belt and Road Initiative** (alleged):
- Finance infrastructure in poor countries
- Countries cannot repay
- China takes control of ports, facilities
- Extends Chinese influence

But Western institutions did this first and continue:
- IMF structural adjustment
- World Bank development projects
- US military aid tied to policy compliance

**Real consequence**:
- Perpetual debt dependency
- Sovereignty compromised
- Resources extracted
- Population bears costs

### Sanctions as Mass Punishment

**Economic sanctions**:

Target government does something US dislikes → US imposes sanctions → economy collapses → population suffers → government often doesn't change behavior.

**Examples**:

**Iraq (1990-2003)**:
- Sanctions killed ~500,000 children (UNICEF estimate)
- Madeleine Albright asked if price worth it: "We think the price is worth it"
- Saddam Hussein remained in power
- Iraqi people suffered for government's actions

**Venezuela (ongoing)**:
- US sanctions
- Economy collapsed
- Hyperinflation
- Medical shortages
- Maduro remains in power
- People starve

**Iran (ongoing)**:
- Sanctions prevent medical imports during COVID
- People die from treatable conditions
- Government doesn't change behavior
- Population punished for government's policies

**Friend-enemy**:
- Target government is enemy
- Civilian population treated as acceptable casualties
- Sanctions are violence, but invisible violence (deaths don't count as killing)

### Military-Industrial Complex: Perpetual War as Profit

**War profiteering**:

Defense contractors profit from war. Therefore:
- Lobby for military spending
- Support hawkish politicians
- Manufacture threats
- Ensure wars continue

**Real mechanism**:
- Lockheed Martin, Boeing, Raytheon donate to politicians
- Politicians approve military budgets
- Wars ensure demand for weapons
- Companies profit from deaths

**Afghanistan War**:
- 20 years, $2 trillion spent
- Defense contractors made billions
- ~200,000 dead (mostly Afghan civilians)
- Taliban back in power (same as 2001)
- War profiteers benefited from failure

Friend-enemy:
- Defense contractors are friends (profit from war)
- Soldiers and civilians are enemies (expendable in pursuit of profit)
- Peace is enemy (reduces profits)

### Arms Sales: Arming Enemies of Enemies

**US arms sales**:

US largest arms exporter. Sells to:
- Saudi Arabia (uses weapons to bomb Yemen, 400,000+ dead)
- Israel (uses weapons against Palestinians)
- Egypt (uses weapons against own population)
- UAE, Qatar, Kuwait, others

This arms dictatorships and enables war crimes. Why?
- Profit for defense contractors
- Geopolitical influence
- Jobs in weapons manufacturing

**Real consequence**:
- US-made weapons kill civilians globally
- US enables humanitarian catastrophes
- Arms sales perpetuate conflicts
- But this is "foreign policy," not mass murder

### NGOs and Humanitarian Intervention: Empire by Other Means

**The NGO-industrial complex**:

Western NGOs operate in Global South providing:
- Aid
- Development
- Democracy promotion
- Human rights advocacy

Sounds benign. Actually often:
- Impose Western values and systems
- Undermine local autonomy
- Create dependency
- Serve Western geopolitical interests

**USAID**: Officially development agency. Actually:
- CIA front in many countries
- Funds regime change operations
- Promotes policies benefiting US corporations
- "Development" means integration into US-led order

**Real example—Bolivia**:

US-funded NGOs supported coup against Evo Morales (2019). Democracy promotion rhetoric. Actual goal: restore neoliberal government friendly to US interests and corporations.

Friend-enemy: Western interests are friends (to be promoted). Governments resisting Western dominance are enemies (to be overthrown, even if democratically elected).

---

## PART VIII: CORPORATE POWER STRUCTURES

### The Corporation as Private Tyranny

**Internal corporate structure**:

Corporation is dictatorship. CEO has absolute power over employees. Board represents shareholders only. Workers have no voice.

This is friend-enemy at micro-level:
- Shareholders are friends (profits distributed to them)
- Workers are enemies (costs to be minimized)
- Customers are enemies (to be extracted from)
- Competitors are enemies (to be destroyed)
- Regulators are enemies (to be captured or evaded)
- Environment is enemy (to be exploited)

**Real consequences**:

Amazon:
- Warehouse workers monitored constantly
- Bathroom breaks timed
- Fired for not meeting quotas
- Injuries common, medical care denied
- Union organizing crushed
- While Bezos became richest man in world

Friend-enemy: Bezos and shareholders benefit from worker suffering. Workers are enemies to be extracted from maximally.

### Monopoly Power: The Power to Eliminate Competition

**When one company controls market**:

They can:
- Set prices arbitrarily
- Degrade service (no alternatives)
- Crush potential competitors
- Capture regulators
- Extract monopoly rents

**Examples**:

**Telecom monopolies**:
- US has among worst internet in developed world
- Highest prices
- Worst service
- Because local monopolies eliminate competition
- Lobby to prevent municipal broadband

**Tech monopolies**:
- Google controls search (90% market share)
- Facebook controls social media
- Amazon controls e-commerce
- Apple/Google control mobile OS

They can:
- Deplatform competitors
- Copy and destroy competitors
- Extract rent from entire ecosystem
- Shape information environment

Friend-enemy: Monopolies treat competitors as enemies to eliminate, customers as enemies to exploit, and regulators as enemies to capture.

### Supply Chain Power: The Power of Chokepoints

**Who controls critical infrastructure**:

Modern economy depends on few companies controlling critical nodes:

**Shipping**: Maersk, MSC, CMA CGM control most container shipping
**Semiconductors**: TSMC produces most advanced chips
**Cloud computing**: AWS, Azure, Google Cloud host most internet
**Payment processing**: Visa, Mastercard process most transactions
**Domain names**: ICANN controls internet naming

Each is chokepoint. Can shut down anyone by denying access.

**Real power**:
- Visa/Mastercard deplatformed WikiLeaks
- AWS deplatformed Parler
- Domain registrars can make websites disappear
- Shipping disruption causes economic crisis

Friend-enemy: Chokepoint controllers decide who gets access. Friends get service; enemies get cut off.

### Franchise and Licensing: Gatekeeping Power

**Professional licensing**:

Want to work as doctor, lawyer, hairstylist, contractor, electrician? Must get license.

Licensing boards controlled by existing practitioners. They can:
- Restrict supply (limit competition)
- Exclude foreigners (even if qualified)
- Require expensive education (class barrier)
- Revoke licenses arbitrarily

This is guild system—insiders protecting their territory from enemies.

**Real consequence**:
- Artificial scarcity raises prices
- Poor people cannot afford services
- Poor people cannot enter professions (educational barriers)
- Licenses protect established practitioners at public expense

**Medical licensing**:

American Medical Association restricts number of doctors (limits medical school slots, restricts foreign doctors). Result:
- Doctor shortage
- Higher medical costs
- Reduced access to care

AMA claims this ensures quality. Actually ensures high incomes for existing doctors at expense of patients.

Friend-enemy: Licensed doctors are friends (protected). Would-be doctors and patients are enemies (excluded, exploited).

### Bankruptcy Law: Power Imbalances in Insolvency

**Corporate vs. personal bankruptcy**:

Corporation cannot pay debts → Chapter 11 bankruptcy:
- Restructure debt
- Continue operating
- Executives keep jobs
- Often emerge profitable

Individual cannot pay debts → Chapter 7/13 bankruptcy:
- Lose assets
- Credit destroyed for years
- Student debt CANNOT be discharged
- Medical debt from illness punished forever

**Real consequence**:
- Corporations get fresh starts
- Individuals crushed by debt permanently
- Student debt made non-dischargeable by lobbying
- This is power protecting corporate friends, punishing individual enemies

**Leveraged buyouts and asset stripping**:

Private equity firm:
- Buys company with borrowed money
- Loads debt onto company
- Extracts dividends
- Company cannot service debt
- Company goes bankrupt
- Workers lose jobs and pensions
- Private equity firm profits

This is legalized looting. But treated as "business strategy."

Friend-enemy: Private equity friends profit. Workers enemies destroyed.

---

## PART IX: SLOW VIOLENCE AND STRUCTURAL DEATH

### The Concept of Slow Violence

Environmental degradation, poverty, malnutrition kill slowly over time. These deaths are:
- Invisible (no dramatic event)
- Diffused (hard to attribute causation)
- Normalized (treated as inevitable)

But they're results of power decisions about who lives and who dies.

**Toxic waste and sacrifice zones**:

Polluting industries locate in poor/minority neighborhoods:
- Cancer rates skyrocket
- Children develop asthma, lead poisoning
- People die years early

Why these neighborhoods? Because:
- Politically powerless (cannot resist)
- Economically desperate (need jobs)
- Racially devalued (Black/Latino lives matter less)

**Real examples**:

**Flint, Michigan**: Government switched water source to save money → pipes leached lead → children permanently brain damaged → officials knew and lied → no one held accountable.

Friend-enemy: White officials protected (escaped consequences). Black residents were enemies (expendable).

**Cancer Alley, Louisiana**: 150-mile stretch of petrochemical plants. Predominantly Black communities. Cancer rates among highest in nation. Companies knew. Continued operating.

**Environmental racism as enemy designation**:

Pollution is not distributed randomly. It's concentrated where people lack power to resist. This is violence:
- Shortens lives
- Destroys health
- Poisons children
- Ruins communities

But invisible violence. Deaths counted as cancer, not as murder by pollution.

Friend-enemy: Corporations profit. Residents are enemies whose health is sacrificed for profit.

### Structural Violence: The Violence of Social Structures

**Johan Galtung's framework**:

Violence is not just direct physical harm. Violence is anything that prevents people from reaching their potential.

**Types**:
- **Direct violence**: Physical harm (murder, assault, war)
- **Structural violence**: Social structures that harm (poverty, inequality, oppression)
- **Cultural violence**: Ideology that legitimizes structural violence

**Poverty as violence**:

When social structures ensure some people starve while others feast:
- This is violence
- Someone is choosing this distribution
- Deaths are not accidental

When children die of preventable diseases because families cannot afford treatment:
- This is violence
- System chose profit over lives
- Deaths are policy outcomes, not unfortunate accidents

**The magnitude**:

Direct violence kills ~600,000/year globally (wars, homicides, etc.)
Structural violence kills ~18 million/year (poverty, preventable disease, malnutrition)

Structural violence kills 30x more than direct violence. But it's invisible. No one prosecuted. Treated as natural.

Friend-enemy: Those who benefit from structures are friends. Those crushed by structures are enemies eliminated through "impersonal forces."

### Necropolitics: The Politics of Death

**Achille Mbembe's concept**:

Sovereignty is not just power over territory or law. Sovereignty is power to determine who lives and who dies.

Modern states exercise necropower:
- Decide which populations are expendable
- Create conditions for mass death
- Permit certain groups to die
- Actively kill others

**Organized abandonment**:

State withdraws from certain populations/territories:
- No public services
- No infrastructure investment
- No police protection (or only oppressive policing)
- No economic development

Result: Population suffers, dies, or is forced to leave.

**Examples**:

**Post-Katrina New Orleans**: 
- Predominantly Black Lower Ninth Ward
- Levees known to be inadequate
- Flood kills ~1,800
- Government response inadequate
- Reconstruction favors wealthy areas
- Poor displaced permanently

This is necropolitics: Black poor designated as enemies worth abandoning to death.

**Rust Belt deindustrialization**:
- Capital flees to cheaper labor
- Jobs disappear
- Communities collapse
- Drug epidemic, suicide epidemic, declining life expectancy
- "Deaths of despair" (Case and Deaton)
- No government intervention

Necropolitics: Working-class whites designated as expendable enemies.

**Colonialism as necropolitical**:

Belgian Congo: Leopold's regime killed ~10 million through:
- Forced labor
- Mutilation
- Starvation
- Disease

Treated as legitimate commercial enterprise. Extraction of rubber required mass death. Indigenous population were enemies whose deaths enriched Belgium.

### Environmental Degradation as Slow-Motion Genocide

**Pollution-caused deaths**:

~9 million die annually from pollution globally (Lancet study). This exceeds deaths from AIDS, malaria, and tuberculosis COMBINED.

These deaths are:
- Concentrated in poor countries
- Caused by rich countries' pollution
- Preventable
- Results of power decisions about whose lungs matter

**Fossil fuel air pollution**:

~5 million annual deaths from fossil fuel particulates. Companies know their products kill. Continue selling. Oppose regulation. Fund denial.

This is mass murder for profit. But treated as "energy policy."

**Toxic chemicals**:

Pesticides, industrial chemicals, plastics cause:
- Cancer
- Endocrine disruption
- Developmental problems
- Reproductive harm

Chemical companies:
- Know dangers
- Suppress research
- Fight regulation
- Continue production

Friend-enemy: Chemical companies profit. Poisoned populations are enemies whose deaths are acceptable.

**Water privatization**:

Corporations privatize water supplies. Raise prices. Poor cannot afford. Result:
- People die of preventable waterborne disease
- Must choose between water and food
- Cholera outbreaks
- All so corporations can profit from necessity

Bolivia (2000): Bechtel privatized water. Prices increased 300%. People couldn't afford. Protests violently suppressed. Eventually reversed.

Friend-enemy: Corporation treating water as commodity. Those who need water but cannot pay are enemies.

---

## PART X: EPISTEMOLOGICAL POWER - CONTROLLING KNOWLEDGE AND PERCEPTION

### Manufacturing Consent: Media as Power

**Propaganda model** (Herman and Chomsky):

Mass media serves power by:
- Filtering out information challenging power
- Amplifying narratives serving power
- Marginalizing dissent
- Manufacturing public consent for elite policies

**Five filters**:
1. Ownership (media owned by wealthy/corporations)
2. Advertising (real customers are advertisers, not readers)
3. Sourcing (rely on official sources—government, corporate PR)
4. Flak (punish media that step out of line)
5. Ideology (anti-communism during Cold War, terrorism now)

**Real consequence**:
- Iraq War: Media amplified WMD lies, marginalized skeptics
- Financial crisis: Media didn't investigate fraud until after crash
- Climate change: Media gave deniers equal time despite no scientific basis
- All cases where media served power against public interest

Friend-enemy: Media are friends of power (symbiotic relationship). Truth-tellers are enemies (marginalized, fired, smeared).

### The Academic-Industrial Complex

**Research funding determines knowledge**:

Who funds research shapes what gets discovered:
- Pharmaceutical companies fund drug research (positive results published, negative results buried)
- Fossil fuel companies fund climate denial
- Tobacco companies funded doubt about cancer
- Sugar industry funded nutrition research blaming fat instead of sugar

**Real mechanism**:
- Industry funds favorable research
- Publishes results supporting their interests
- Suppresses unfavorable research
- Captures regulatory agencies with industry-funded "science"

**Consequence**:
- Decades of delay recognizing dangers
- Millions harmed/killed while industry profited
- Public health sacrificed to corporate profit

**Academic gatekeeping**:

Who gets to be academic?
- Expensive education (class barrier)
- Unpaid internships (class barrier)
- Publish or perish (favors those with institutional support)
- Peer review by insiders (reproduces existing paradigms)

Result: Knowledge production controlled by those already powerful.

Friend-enemy: Credentialed insiders are friends. Outsiders are enemies whose knowledge doesn't count.

### Psychiatric Power: The Power to Define Sanity

**Labeling as social control**:

Who counts as mentally ill? Psychiatry has historically labeled as pathological:
- Homosexuality (until 1973)
- Women wanting education (hysteria)
- Slaves wanting freedom (drapetomania)
- Soviet dissidents (sluggish schizophrenia)

**Current uses**:
- Pathologize resistance ("oppositional defiant disorder")
- Drug children into compliance (ADHD overdiagnosis)
- Involuntary commitment of inconvenient people
- Forced medication

**Friend-enemy**:
- Those who conform are sane (friends)
- Those who resist are insane (enemies to be medicated/confined)
- Psychiatry as tool of social control

### Statistical Power: The Power of Metrics

**What gets measured determines what gets valued**:

GDP measures:
- Economic activity
- Doesn't distinguish between good (healthcare) and bad (pollution cleanup after disaster)
- Doesn't count:
  - Unpaid care work (mostly women)
  - Environmental destruction
  - Inequality
  - Well-being

Result: Policies optimize GDP even when this harms actual welfare.

**Real consequence**:
- Environmental destruction increases GDP (economic activity from extraction and cleanup)
- War increases GDP (weapons manufacturing, reconstruction)
- Caregiving decreases GDP (if unpaid)
- System optimizes for wrong metric

**Crime statistics**:

Police department measured by arrests. Result:
- Incentive to arrest
- Broken windows policing
- Target easy arrests (poor, minority)
- Mass incarceration

If metric was "reduced crime," incentives different. If metric was "community well-being," entirely different policing.

Friend-enemy: Metrics serve power's interests. What gets measured makes certain populations enemies (those needing help become problems to be eliminated from statistics).

### Educational Testing as Sorting Mechanism

**Standardized tests**:

SAT/ACT claim to measure merit. Actually measure:
- Access to test prep (rich can afford)
- Quality of schooling (rich neighborhoods)
- Cultural capital (tests biased toward dominant culture)
- Test-taking skills (can be taught, expensive)

Result: Tests reproduce existing inequality while appearing meritocratic.

**Real consequence**:
- College admissions based on tests
- Tests favor wealthy students
- System legitimizes inequality ("they tested better" not "they had advantages")
- Poor and minority students labeled as less capable

Friend-enemy: Tests designate rich students as friends (merit badges). Poor students as enemies (justifiably excluded).

**IQ testing**:

Originally developed to identify students needing help. Weaponized to:
- Justify racial hierarchies
- Sterilize "feeble-minded"
- Restrict immigration
- Track students into different educational paths

Tests claimed to measure innate ability. Actually measured:
- Cultural knowledge
- Educational opportunities
- Language familiarity
- Test-taking experience

But used to permanently label some as inferior.

Friend-enemy: Those who test well are friends (intelligent, deserving). Those who don't are enemies (undeserving, excludable).

---

## PART XI: TEMPORAL VIOLENCE - THE POWER TO STEAL FUTURES

### Intergenerational Theft

**Climate change as violence against future people**:

Present generation extracts wealth through:
- Burning fossil fuels
- Deforesting
- Depleting aquifers
- Destroying biodiversity
- Polluting oceans

Results:
- Habitable planet for us now
- Uninhabitable planet for future generations

This is theft from future people. They will suffer so we can consume. But future people cannot resist—they don't exist yet.

**Real consequence**:
- We are consuming their inheritance
- They will face climate catastrophe
- They will hate us for what we've done
- But we benefit now; they suffer later

Friend-enemy: Present people (especially rich) are friends to each other. Future people are enemies whose world we're destroying.

**National debt as intergenerational warfare**:

Government borrows to fund present consumption. Future generations must repay.

US national debt ~$33 trillion. Who borrowed? Mostly for:
- Tax cuts for rich
- Wars
- Bank bailouts

Who repays? Future workers.

This is stealing from future people to benefit present powerful.

### The Power to Deny Future

**Who gets a future?**:

Poor children:
- Attend underfunded schools
- Live in polluted neighborhoods
- Lack access to healthcare
- Face criminal justice system
- Burdened with debt
- Statistically will remain poor

Rich children:
- Attend elite schools
- Live in clean, safe neighborhoods
- Access best healthcare
- Shielded from criminal justice
- Inherit wealth
- Statistically will remain rich

**Real mechanism**:
- System reproduces inequality across generations
- Poor children's futures stolen before they're born
- Rich children's futures secured before they're born
- "Meritocracy" legitimizes this theft

**The future as contested terrain**:

Who gets to have children? Who gets to raise them? Who gets to shape what future looks like?

**Reproductive control**: 
- Abortion restrictions prevent poor women from controlling reproductive timing
- Forced sterilization prevents "undesirable" populations from reproducing
- Adoption laws favor wealthy couples
- Foster system warehouses poor children

**Educational access**:
- Elite education produces future leaders
- Poor education produces future workers/prisoners
- System ensures class reproduction

**Environmental destruction**:
- Some people's children will inherit wealth
- Some people's children will inherit toxic wasteland
- Not random which children get which future

Friend-enemy: Powerful ensure their children have futures. Weak's children are enemies whose futures are stolen.

---

## PART XII: RESISTANCE TO POWER - HOW THE DESIGNATED ENEMIES FIGHT BACK

### Sabotage: The Weapon of the Weak

When you cannot fight openly, you sabotage:

**Historical examples**:

**Enslaved people**:
- Broke tools
- Worked slowly
- Feigned ignorance
- Poisoned masters' food
- Burned crops/property
- Ran away

Each act of sabotage:
- Small reduction in master's power
- Assertion of agency despite bondage
- Risky but sometimes only resistance possible

**Factory workers**:
- Luddites smashed machines
- Workers slow production
- "Work to rule" (follow every regulation exactly, grinds productivity)
- Strikes and walkouts
- Whistleblowing

**Environmental sabotage**:
- Tree spiking (prevents logging)
- Equipment sabotage (stops pipeline construction)
- Blockades (prevent resource extraction)

Each case: Designated enemies using available means to resist those with power.

**The debate**:
- Is property destruction violence?
- If corporation is slowly killing you, is sabotaging their equipment legitimate self-defense?
- Pacifists say no violence ever justified
- But structural violence kills more than direct violence

### Riots and Uprisings: Collective Violence of the Powerless

**When peaceful means fail**:

People protest peacefully for change. Demands ignored. What next?

**Historical pattern**:
- Civil rights movement: Peaceful protests met with violence, limited gains
- Riots (Watts, Detroit, Newark) → suddenly government responds
- MLK: "Riot is language of the unheard"

**The friend-enemy of rioting**:

Power frames riots as:
- Senseless violence
- Criminal behavior
- Proof that rioters are enemies of civilization

Rioters experience it as:
- Justified response to oppression
- Only language power understands
- Destruction of property that symbolizes exploitation

**Property vs. people**:

During riots, power prioritizes property over lives:
- Police use lethal force to protect property
- Insurance replaces property damage
- But lives lost by state violence are not replaceable

This reveals the values: Property (friends) protected; rioters (enemies) killed.

**Looting as redistribution**:

When poor people take from stores during unrest, power calls it "looting" (crime).

Rioters often see it as:
- Reclaiming stolen wealth
- Temporary redistribution
- Just compensation for systemic theft

Perspective: Is it theft to take from those who've stolen from you?

### Revolutionary Violence: Taking Power by Force

**When is revolutionary violence justified?**

If system is:
- Killing you through structural violence
- Prevents peaceful change
- Offers no alternative

Is violent revolution self-defense?

**The oppressor's peace vs. the oppressor's violence**:

Oppressed people are told: "Violence is wrong. Change things peacefully."

But:
- System uses violence constantly (police, military, economic coercion)
- System prevents peaceful change
- System kills through structural violence

So oppressor's message is: "Submit to our violence. Don't resist violently."

**Friend-enemy**:
- Oppressor violence is legitimate ("maintaining order")
- Oppressed violence is illegitimate ("terrorism," "riot," "crime")
- This asymmetry is power

**Historical success of revolutionary violence**:

- Haitian Revolution: Enslaved people killed slaveholders, won freedom
- French Revolution: Overthrew aristocracy (though devoured its children)
- October Revolution: Overthrew Tsar (though became totalitarian)
- Chinese Revolution: Overthrew landlords and KMT
- Cuban Revolution: Overthrew Batista
- Anti-colonial movements: Drove out empires through violent resistance

Counter-argument: Many failed. Many succeeded only to become oppressive themselves. Violence tends to reproduce itself.

But: Would Haitians have won freedom peacefully? Would decolonization have happened without armed struggle?

### Mass Strikes and Withdrawal of Labor

**The general strike**:

When workers collectively refuse to work:
- Economy stops
- Power must negotiate
- Workers demonstrate their actual power

**Historical examples**:

**1968 France**:
- General strike
- Country paralyzed
- De Gaulle nearly overthrown
- Significant concessions won

**Contemporary strikes**:
- Teachers' strikes for better schools
- Amazon workers walking out
- Gig workers demanding rights

Each demonstrates: Labor is actual source of value. Capital needs labor more than labor needs capital.

**The power revealed**:

Normal operation obscures that workers create value. Strike reveals that capital without labor is powerless.

Friend-enemy: Capitalists want workers docile. Strikes reveal workers can be enemies who paralyze system.

### Mutual Aid: Building Alternative Power

**When designated enemies help each other**:

If system treats you as enemy to be eliminated, survival requires mutual aid:

**Black Panther Party**:
- Free breakfast for children
- Free healthcare clinics
- Community defense against police
- "Survival programs pending revolution"

**Real mechanism**:
- Meet needs system refuses to meet
- Build alternative institutions
- Create solidarity
- Demonstrate system's failure

Power's response: Destroy mutual aid institutions (FBI crushed Black Panthers).

Why? Because mutual aid:
- Reduces dependency on system
- Builds alternative power base
- Shows another world is possible
- Threatens existing order

Friend-enemy: Mutual aid transforms enemies (atomized, dependent individuals) into friends (collective, self-sufficient communities).

---

## PART XIII: THE FRIEND-ENEMY MATRIX - COMPREHENSIVE POWER MAPPING

### Every Domain Analyzed Through Friend-Enemy

For every social domain, ask:
1. Who has power?
2. Whose interests conflict?
3. Who benefits from whose harm?
4. Who can harm with impunity?
5. Who is expendable?

**Healthcare Domain**:
- Friends: Insurance companies, pharmaceutical companies, hospital corporations, wealthy patients
- Enemies: Poor patients, uninsured, chronically ill, disabled
- Power mechanism: Ability to deny care
- Real consequence: ~68,000 annual preventable deaths

**Housing Domain**:
- Friends: Landlords, developers, banks, real estate investors
- Enemies: Tenants, homeless, poor
- Power mechanism: Ability to evict, raise rents, gentrify
- Real consequence: ~600,000 homeless, thousands of deaths from exposure

**Employment Domain**:
- Friends: Employers, shareholders, executives
- Enemies: Workers, unemployed, disabled
- Power mechanism: Ability to hire/fire, set wages, determine conditions
- Real consequence: Poverty, overwork, workplace deaths

**Education Domain**:
- Friends: Wealthy students, credentialed professionals, elite institutions
- Enemies: Poor students, uneducated, alternative knowledges
- Power mechanism: Gatekeeping credentialing, student debt, tracking
- Real consequence: Reproduction of class hierarchy

**Criminal Justice Domain**:
- Friends: Police, prosecutors, prison corporations, political advocates of "tough on crime"
- Enemies: Poor, minorities, formerly incarcerated, addicted
- Power mechanism: Arrest, prosecution, incarceration, parole
- Real consequence: 2.3 million incarcerated, families destroyed

**Immigration Domain**:
- Friends: Citizens, border enforcement, detention corporations
- Enemies: Immigrants, refugees, undocumented
- Power mechanism: Borders, detention, deportation
- Real consequence: Thousands dead at borders, families separated

**Environment Domain**:
- Friends: Polluting industries, resource extractors, consumers in wealthy countries
- Enemies: Indigenous people, poor communities near pollution, future generations
- Power mechanism: Externalization of costs, regulatory capture
- Real consequence: Millions dead from pollution, climate catastrophe

**Gender Domain**:
- Friends: Men, patriarchal system beneficiaries
- Enemies: Women, gender non-conforming, feminists
- Power mechanism: Violence, economic discrimination, reproductive control
- Real consequence: Domestic violence, wage gap, forced pregnancy

**Racial Domain**:
- Friends: White people, white supremacist system
- Enemies: People of color, anti-racist activists
- Power mechanism: Police violence, discrimination, segregation, mass incarceration
- Real consequence: Systematic oppression, shortened lives, stolen wealth

### The Intersection: Multiple Enemy Designations

**Most oppressed face multiple enemy designations simultaneously**:

Poor, Black, disabled woman faces:
- Class enemy designation (poor = lazy, undeserving)
- Racial enemy designation (Black = dangerous, criminal)
- Gender enemy designation (woman = inferior, sexual object)
- Disability enemy designation (disabled = burden, worthless)

Each system of power marks her as enemy:
- Capitalism: Not profitable to employ
- White supremacy: Dangerous other
- Patriarchy: Inferior being
- Ableism: Defective specimen

Result: Multiply oppressed, multiply designated as enemy, multiply harmed.

This is why intersectionality matters—you cannot understand oppression without understanding how multiple enemy-designations compound.

### The Alliance Map: Who Can Be Friends?

Against multiple systems of power, who can ally?

**Class unity**:
- All workers exploited by capital
- But divided by race, gender, nationality
- Cross-racial, cross-gender working-class unity possible but difficult
- Requires white workers and male workers to surrender privileges

**Racial unity**:
- All people of color face white supremacy
- But divided by class, gender, specific ethnicity
- Cross-class racial unity possible but difficult
- Requires bourgeois POC to choose racial solidarity over class interest

**Gender unity**:
- All women face patriarchy
- But divided by class, race, sexuality
- Cross-class, cross-race women's unity possible but difficult
- Requires privileged women to choose gender solidarity over other privileges

**The problem**: Power divides potential allies. Each identity category contains class divisions. Each class contains identity divisions.

**The solution?**: Intersectional solidarity recognizing:
- Multiple systems of oppression
- Multiple enemy designations
- Need for coalitions across differences
- While acknowledging power differences within coalition

---

## PART XIV: THE POWER TO DEFINE REALITY ITSELF

### Who Decides What Counts as Real?

**The ultimate power**:

Not just power over bodies or resources. Power to determine what counts as real, true, important, valuable.

**Consensus reality**:

Society agrees on:
- What is true (science, news, common sense)
- What is valuable (money, credentials, status)
- What is possible (capitalism is inevitable, human nature is selfish)
- What is desirable (wealth, beauty, success)

But this consensus serves power:
- Makes existing order seem natural
- Makes alternatives seem impossible
- Makes resistance seem futile or insane

**Hegemony**: When oppressed internalize oppressor's worldview as reality itself.

**Breaking the reality monopoly**:

Resistance requires asserting alternative realities:
- "Another world is possible"
- "Capitalism is not inevitable"
- "Human nature is cooperative"
- "We can change this"

But asserting alternative realities makes you:
- Crazy (dismissed as delusional)
- Dangerous (threat to consensus)
- Enemy (subverting "reality")

**Gaslighting as political strategy**:

Power denies your lived experience:
- "Police aren't racist" (when you've experienced police racism)
- "System is meritocratic" (when you've seen mediocre rich succeed)
- "Markets are fair" (when you've been exploited)

This makes you doubt your own perceptions. Most insidious form of power—makes you question your own reality.

### The Overton Window: The Power to Limit Possibility

**What ideas are acceptable?**:

Political discourse has window of acceptable ideas. Ideas outside window are "extremist," "unrealistic," "radical."

**Who sets window?**:
- Media (owned by wealthy)
- Political parties (funded by wealthy)
- Think tanks (funded by wealthy)
- Academic institutions (influenced by wealthy donors)

Result: Window includes only ideas that don't threaten power.

**Example shifts**:

**Healthcare**:
- Within window: Minor tweaks to ACA, limited public option
- Outside window: Universal single-payer healthcare (despite majority support and working in other countries)

Why? Because single-payer threatens:
- Insurance industry profits
- Pharmaceutical pricing power
- Medical industry rent-extraction

**Climate**:
- Within window: Carbon taxes, green technology, market solutions
- Outside window: Rapid phase-out of fossil fuels, economic transformation, degrowth

Why? Because transformation threatens fossil capital.

**Overton window as enemy designation**:

Ideas outside window are "extremist." Those advocating them are "radicals" (enemies).

This is power:
- Determining what can be discussed
- Who gets platform
- What alternatives are imaginable

### Manufacturing Necessity: "There Is No Alternative"

**TINA—Thatcher's dictum**:

"There is no alternative" to capitalism, markets, austerity, etc.

This is ultimate power move:
- Present political choice as natural necessity
- Make resistance seem futile
- Depoliticize by presenting as technical/inevitable

**Real mechanism**:

IMF tells country: "You must accept austerity. No alternative."
- Actually: Alternative is defaulting on debt, redistributing wealth, expropriating capital
- But these alternatives not offered
- TINA conceals that these are political choices benefiting creditors

**Breaking TINA**:

Resistance requires asserting: There ARE alternatives.
- Venezuela defaulted, survived
- Iceland prosecuted bankers, recovered better
- Bolivia expelled US, nationalized resources, reduced poverty

Each example proves TINA is lie. Alternatives exist. Power wants you to believe they don't.

---

## PART XV: THE MOST COMPREHENSIVE FRIEND-ENEMY-POWER ANALYSIS EVER

### The Ultimate Friend-Enemy Taxonomy

**Across every dimension of human existence**:

1. **Economic**: Rich vs. poor, owners vs. workers, creditors vs. debtors, landlords vs. tenants
2. **Political**: Rulers vs. ruled, citizens vs. foreigners, loyalists vs. dissidents
3. **Racial**: Dominant races vs. subordinated races, colonizers vs. colonized
4. **Gender**: Men vs. women, cis vs. trans, straight vs. queer
5. **Ability**: Abled vs. disabled, neurotypical vs. neurodivergent
6. **Age**: Adults vs. children, young vs. old
7. **Religious**: Believers vs. infidels, orthodox vs. heretics
8. **National**: Citizens vs. foreigners, nationals vs. immigrants
9. **Linguistic**: Dominant language speakers vs. others
10. **Educational**: Credentialed vs. uncredentialed, literate vs. illiterate
11. **Geographic**: Urban vs. rural, core vs. periphery, North vs. South
12. **Temporal**: Present vs. future generations
13. **Species**: Humans vs. non-humans (animals, environment)
14. **Technological**: Digital natives vs. excluded, enhanced vs. natural
15. **Epistemological**: Experts vs. lay people, knowers vs. ignorant

Each dimension has friend-enemy structure. Each creates power relations. Each produces real consequences.

### The Compound Effect: Multiple Enemy Designations

Being designated enemy in multiple dimensions creates:
- Multiply oppressed (intersectionality)
- Compound disadvantages
- Shortened lifespan
- Reduced opportunities
- Systematic exclusion

**Most oppressed**:

Poor, Black, disabled, queer, immigrant, woman faces:
- Economic exploitation
- Racial violence
- Disability discrimination
- Homophobia/transphobia
- Immigration persecution
- Gender oppression

Each system marks her as enemy. Combined effect is:
- Extreme precarity
- Constant threat
- Multiple simultaneous oppressions
- Shortened life expectancy
- Limited options

**Most privileged**:

Rich, white, abled, straight, citizen, man experiences:
- Economic extraction ability (not exploitation)
- Racial privilege
- Ability privilege
- Heterosexual privilege
- Citizenship privilege
- Male privilege

Each system marks him as friend. Combined effect is:
- Extreme security
- Protected from violence
- Multiple simultaneous privileges
- Extended life expectancy
- Unlimited options

The difference in lived experience is not incremental—it's qualitatively different worlds.

### The 20-Year Life Expectancy Gap

**Material consequences of friend-enemy designation**:

Life expectancy varies by ~20+ years between most and least privileged:
- Poor Black men in certain neighborhoods: ~60 years
- Rich white men in wealthy neighborhoods: ~85 years

This 25-year gap is result of:
- Accumulated effects of oppression across all domains
- Systematic marking as enemy in multiple dimensions
- Material deprivation
- Stress and violence
- Lack of access to health resources
- Environmental toxins
- Police violence
- Incarceration

This is not genetic or personal failing. This is power.

**Each year of lost life is**:
- Result of concrete power relations
- Benefit to those whose lives are extended
- (Rich live longer partly because poor die younger—resource distribution)

### The Global Scale: International Friend-Enemy

**Core-Periphery extraction**:

Global North extracts ~$2 trillion/year from Global South through:
- Unequal exchange (undervalued labor/resources)
- Debt service
- Profit repatriation
- Tax evasion
- Land grabs
- Brain drain

**Real consequence**:

If this wealth stayed in Global South:
- Poverty could be eliminated
- Healthcare accessible
- Infrastructure developed
- Education universal

But North extracts it. South remains poor. Not accident—design.

Friend-enemy: North treats South as enemy to be exploited. Extraction is violence. Deaths from poverty in South are results of Northern enrichment.

### The Species Scale: Anthropocene as War Against Future Life

**Current generation vs. all future life**:

Our extraction/pollution:
- Uses resources future generations need
- Destroys biodiversity
- Destabilizes climate
- Poisons soil/water/air

We're at war with:
- Our descendants
- Other species
- Future life itself

And we're winning (short-term). But victory means everyone loses (long-term).

This is most absolute enemy designation possible: Treating all future life as enemy worth sacrificing for present profit.
